Commentary

Sincere Reflections on the Completion of the Dike Project

Last year, a flood caused devastation, with dikes and water conservancy projects in the provinces along the Yangtze River collapsing. The floodwaters swept across the land, causing widespread destruction. The National Government's Flood Relief Committee, in order to provide fundamental relief, not only provided emergency relief but also implemented work relief measures to repair various sections of the dikes. Now that the project has been completed, we reflect on the tragic situation of last year when massive waves engulfed everything and people and animals perished together. Seeing the successful completion of this great water conservancy project, we cannot help but feel extremely fortunate.

In the past, when we talked about the great buildings in our country, we would always mention the Great Wall. In fact, the function of the Great Wall in the Qin Dynasty was limited to defending against the Hu, and in recent times, its function has become even less visible. Moreover, its construction was built on the flesh and blood of ordinary people, a fortress to defend "one family's empire," attempting to maintain the inheritance of their descendants for ten thousand generations, and cannot escape the blame of countless generations to come. However, the current water conservancy project spans over 4,390 kilometers, passing through the Yangtze River, Min River, Xiang River, Yuan River, Huai River, Grand Canal, and other river basins in six provinces. Its grandeur is no less than that of the Great Wall, and its importance to the survival of tens of millions of people along the river is even more evident than the Great Wall of one family. This summer and autumn, the floodwaters were also great, but they did not cause a disaster. The greatness of the effectiveness of this thousands of miles of water conservancy project is even more evident. Work relief not only provided an opportunity for thousands of people who were lying down waiting to die and relying on relief to survive to support themselves, but also allowed the formerly intermittent dikes to be integrated into a unified plan, resulting in a greater effect. In the past, whenever a disaster occurred, we only focused on "relief." From the lesson of this work relief, we now understand that the way to provide disaster relief lies not only in "relief," but also in "work."

The Flood Relief Committee has invited people from all walks of life in Shanghai to participate in the dike construction completion ceremony in the capital today, and then to visit various project areas to inspect them. The Flood Relief Committee's huge expenses mostly came from social donations. Now that the project has been completed, those who enthusiastically donated in the past can personally inspect and witness that their donations have been transformed into a great project and have not been wasted. However, we believe that this matter is extremely important, and that this great construction during the national crisis after the great disaster has even deeper significance. Therefore, the Flood Relief Committee's invitation to various sectors to inspect is not to show off its achievements, and those who are invited to inspect also have a different meaning from ordinary tourism. We believe that this trip is deeply related to the water conservancy and people's livelihood of the provinces in the Yangtze River basin in the future.

We believe that the rolling river has fertile land on both sides. If irrigation is proper and the dikes are well maintained, then this rolling river will be enough to benefit the country and the people. However, because irrigation is improper and there are even no water conservancy projects to speak of, last year's flood caused the most severely affected area to reach 265,000 square kilometers, and the less affected area was also around 60,000 square kilometers, which is about the size of England or the state of New York. The affected population was at least 50 million, and many were homeless. Most countries in the world that are lower than the water level have been able to avoid disasters because they focus on water conservancy. Only our country has no choice but to wait for death when a flood comes. We still cannot help but shed tears when we recall the tragic situation of the country being submerged last year. Although the dike project has been completed, we can have some protection, but we still cannot have the idea of ​​"one labor for permanent peace" and think that we have something to rely on and are not afraid. Building a dike is difficult, and preventing dike failure is also difficult. Building a dike is an urgent task, and preventing dike failure is also important. Building but not preventing, or not being good at guarding, will mean that the dike project will be unimaginable in three or two years due to natural erosion. Therefore, in the future, we must carefully study the two issues of how to permanently maintain the dike project and how to use the dike project. Only by being able to use the dikes can the dike project not be abandoned, and only by being able to maintain the dikes can this great project last for a long time.

We are deeply fortunate for the completion of this great project, and we extend our sincere hopes to the government authorities and the gentlemen who are invited to inspect.

The Franco-Russian Non-Aggression Pact Successfully Concluded

Has Been Approved by the French Cabinet and is Scheduled to be Signed Tomorrow

Content Provisions

Mutual respect for territory and possessions, non-resort to war, neutrality in the event of aggression, suppression of boycott, and termination of propaganda

Concentrating Efforts on Commercial Treaty Negotiations in the Future

Reuters, Paris, 26th—The French cabinet today approved the Franco-Russian Non-Aggression Treaty, stipulating: ㈠ Respect for each other's territories, including colonies and protectorates; ㈡ Neither party shall engage in war; ㈢ If either party is subjected to aggression by a third party, the other party must remain neutral; ㈣ Suppression of boycott activities; ㈤ Termination of propaganda, especially through news forms. The Russian government guarantees not to promote or support anti-French propaganda and agitation. The treaty's wording prohibits Soviet Russia from supporting Russian revolutionary organizations within and outside the country that are detrimental to Annam, Syria, and North Africa. This treaty was concluded in Paris today and will be signed on Tuesday.

Havas, Paris, 26th—The Mutual Non-Aggression Treaty between France and Soviet Russia was provisionally initialed on August 24th of last year by the Secretary-General of the French Foreign Ministry and the Soviet Russian Ambassador to France. This morning, Premier Herriot presented the treaty to the Council of State for discussion. The treaty begins with a preamble declaring that the treaty safeguards the League of Nations Covenant and reaffirms the Paris Peace Pact. Following the preamble, there are seven articles stipulating that the non-aggression pledge applies not only to France and its colonies but also to French protectorates and territories under French mandate from the League of Nations. Secondly, both countries mutually prohibit financial and economic boycotts, as well as propaganda activities that politically and socially harm the other country. Furthermore, neither contracting party shall tolerate the existence of any military organization within its territory that aims to attack the other contracting party by force. Additionally, Russian intellectual and mutual aid groups within France shall continue to enjoy the protection afforded to those exiled abroad due to political issues. This Non-Aggression Treaty is modeled after the German-Russian Treaty, with improvements. The non-aggression treaty also includes a conciliation treaty, as Soviet Russia, due to its different political system, is unwilling to recognize the arbitration system and wishes to submit disputes that may arise between the two countries to a conciliation body for review. This body has various powers, including the appointment of experts and the provision of recommendations to the governments concerned. Its nature is similar to the Bryan Commission organized after 1910 when the United States had not yet recognized the principle of arbitration. It is noted that France and Soviet Russia still need to conduct commercial negotiations. The signing of this mutual non-aggression treaty will not hinder the success of commercial negotiations. If political and commercial issues are intertwined, it is difficult to gain an accurate understanding of the various elements of each issue. Separate negotiations can avoid this drawback. France and Russia are signing a non-aggression treaty while proceeding with commercial negotiations, completely separating the two matters. Now that the political issue has been resolved, it will be easier to concentrate on commercial treaty negotiations in the future.

Havas, Paris, 26th—The Franco-Russian Mutual Non-Aggression Treaty was passed by the Council of State this morning. Since 1922, most European countries have been negotiating and concluding mutual non-aggression treaties. The conclusion of the French treaty marks the end of such negotiations, and Europe's "Non-Aggression Treaty" policy has been successfully completed. Between 1925 and 1927, the Moscow government successively concluded friendship treaties or mutual non-aggression treaties with Turkey, Germany, Afghanistan, Lithuania, and Persia. Furthermore, Soviet Russia believed that the Non-War Pact would take a long time to implement. Therefore, in 1928, it suggested to neighboring countries that they conclude a special treaty, with the signatory countries agreeing to implement the Paris Non-War Pact. In 1929, Soviet Russia, Poland, Romania, and the Baltic countries signed this special treaty in Moscow. In 1930, the Soviet Russian government again expressed its willingness to conclude a special treaty with Poland and France, and negotiations immediately commenced. As a result, mutual non-aggression treaties were signed with Finland, Estonia, and Latvia in early 1932 and ratified. In January 1932, Poland provisionally initialed its mutual non-aggression treaty with Russia, which was formally signed in July but not immediately ratified, allowing Romania sufficient time to negotiate a similar treaty with Soviet Russia. However, negotiations between Romania and Soviet Russia failed due to a dispute over the territory of Bessarabia. Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu declared to the Romanian Parliament that Romania still hoped that its allies could sign a mutual non-aggression treaty with Soviet Russia according to the planned schedule. Therefore, French Premier Herriot believed that the Franco-Russian mutual non-aggression treaty, which had already been initialed, should be formally signed at this time and should not be delayed any further. Moreover, Soviet Russia declared to the French government that it would adopt a policy of understanding and would not use violence to resolve the dispute with Romania. Therefore, France had an even greater need to sign the non-aggression treaty. In the same declaration, the Romanian Foreign Minister also requested France to mediate with Romania, so that Soviet Russia would allow Romania to sign a mutual non-aggression treaty with Soviet Russia, based on the foundation agreed upon by Soviet Russian Foreign Commissar Litvinov and Romanian Minister to Paris, Gafencu, within four months from the date of signing the Franco-Russian treaty. The numerous negotiations conducted by a large part of Europe to build peace have now come to an end. We still recall that until now, there has been only one political treaty signed between Russia and a major European power, namely the Treaty of Berlin, concluded between the two countries after the German-Russian Treaty of Rapallo in 1922 (1926). The Treaty of Berlin stipulated that Russia would remain neutral if Germany were attacked. This time, the Franco-Russian treaty stipulates that Russia would remain neutral if France were attacked. The two treaties complement each other and can add another layer of credibility and guarantee to Europe. In view of this point, the importance of the Franco-Russian mutual non-aggression treaty can be imagined.

Romania Abandons Treaty with Russia

Polish-Soviet Treaty Also to be Ratified

Havas, Paris, 26th—It is reported that the Polish government will ratify the Polish-Soviet Mutual Non-Aggression Treaty tomorrow. Furthermore, Romania has abandoned its intention to sign a mutual non-aggression treaty with Soviet Russia. In an effort to remedy the situation, the Soviet Union, at the request of the French government, will attach a special declaration to the aforementioned two treaties.

Havas, Rome, 26th—Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu stated to our correspondent, "Romania is delighted to hear that the Franco-Russian Mutual Non-Aggression Treaty will soon be signed. The rapprochement between France, Poland, and the Soviet Union is extremely beneficial to Romania. As for Romania not concluding a mutual non-aggression treaty with the Soviet Union, it will not have any impact on Romania's alliances with other countries or the friendly relations between Russia and other countries, because Romania loves peace and there is a Non-War Pact."

New Governor-General of the Free State

British Emperor Appoints Buckley

Reuters, Dublin, 26th—The British Emperor has appointed Buckley as the Governor-General of the Irish Free State. The people of the Irish Free State find this appointment quite unexpected. Buckley participated in the revolution in 1916 and was later arrested. He was released during the general amnesty of that year. As a member of the Irish Parliament, Buckley voted against accepting the Anglo-Irish Treaty. In last year's election, Buckley was not elected and has since been engaged in business. An official at the London Free State office told Reuters today that the new Governor-General is respected by people of all levels in Ireland. Buckley will soon meet the British Emperor at Buckingham Palace. He took the oath of allegiance somewhere near Dublin today. It has not yet been decided whether he will reside in the Governor-General's residence. Buckley will receive a full salary of £10,000 but may return part of it.

Wartime Cloaking Device

Using Optics to Invent Steel Armor

The Result of Four Years of Research by a Spanish Engineer

Havas, Madrid, 27th—The Min Sheng Bao reports that the new invention of engineer Olmedo is about to be formally tested. This invention is a steel armor that can make soldiers invisible to the enemy. The method uses a mirror, placed at a specific angle in front of the soldier or equipment to be hidden. The mirror reflects a portion of the ground in front of the mirror, so that the enemy only sees a piece of land and not the soldier or equipment hidden behind the mirror. According to Olmedo, it took four years of research to achieve this result, inspired by the mimicking abilities of certain animals, such as chameleons.

British Cabinet Meets Today

Discussing War Debt Issue

Reply to the US in Drafting

Details Reasons for Requesting Deferred Payment

France and Belgium Also Express

Inability to Pay Due US Debt

Reuters, London, 26th—The cabinet will likely meet on Sunday to discuss the war debt issue. Prime Minister MacDonald will first hold informal talks with Foreign Secretary Simon and Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain tomorrow. According to reliable sources, a draft of the British reply can be submitted to the Prime Minister for review tomorrow. The document will detail Britain's reasons for requesting a deferral of the debt due in December, in preparation for revising the entire war debt. If the war debt issue across the Atlantic is not first studied, the facts will compel a renewed discussion of the reparations issue and the war debt issue, resulting in the harm and unexpected changes that the Lausanne Conference has already eliminated. The result will delay the recovery of global commerce. Yesterday, Chamberlain stated that in this second note, Britain will detail the reasons for requesting a deferral. President Hoover has acknowledged that requesting free discussion of the debt issue is reasonable, so Mr. Hoover apparently does not oppose using this method to reopen the war debt for discussion. Chamberlain expressed satisfaction on this point. As for the final attitude of the US Congress on the issue of deferring next month's debt payment or on the larger debt itself, it is not yet possible to make rash judgments. Well-informed newspapers all acknowledge that negotiations with the US on the issue of next month's payment are unrelated to Britain's ability to pay, but are related to whether the US should accept this payment. The Times' reporter explicitly stated that this issue is of great importance and is not only related to Britain but to the entire world. The Manchester Guardian believes that even if this clause is not included in Britain's new note, it will serve as the background for the overall situation. This payment is indeed sufficient to hinder the recovery of global prosperity, just as the reduced reparations are now being paid. The newspaper concluded that its recent impact will be fluctuating exchange rates, further downward pressure on prices, the Lausanne Agreement becoming waste paper, and the world economic conference being plunged into danger.

Le Matin, Paris, 26th—The government recently announced that it expects a shortfall of 56 billion francs at the end of the current fiscal year, and newspapers are using this as a reason to oppose paying the US debt due on December 15th.

Le Matin, Brussels, 27th—According to responsible sources here, the Belgian government intends to send a note to the US State Department stating that the Belgian government is completely unable to pay the war debt due on December 15th. The Belgian government regrets that the US government has refused to extend the deadline. Even if the US does not collect this payment, it will not be hindered. However, this must wait until the British and French governments decide on the war debt before deciding whether to issue it.

Reuters, Washington, 26th—The US replies to Poland and Czechoslovakia's requests for deferral of war debts were sent out today. The gist is the same as the replies sent to Britain, France, and Belgium: neither extending the deferral period nor agreeing to consider it, but only stating that the US President will ask Congress to re-examine the main issue of war debts.

US "Wet" Faction Rises

Japanese Petty Tricks to Deceive the League of Nations

Forcing Various Groups to Send Telegrams Opposing the Report

Even Elementary School Students are Assigned One Per Grade

Heilongjiang Correspondence: Although Japan is chanting that the League of Nations has no power and that Japan will proceed with its established policy regarding the League of Nations Council convened in Geneva on October 21st, on the other hand, apart from the ruffians in the Northeast who are lawless and engage in open bribery for profit, the Japanese who have some knowledge hold a calm attitude, neither involving themselves in politics nor investing in businesses. When asked why, they reply that the current situation has not yet reached a stable point and that everything is a transitional era. If "Manchukuo" does not face any major difficulties and can be maintained permanently, then the people currently serving in Manchuria are not dispatched by the government and will naturally be replaced. If there are changes in the future, then whether or not to be active at this time is irrelevant. This proves that the Japanese attitude is completely strong on the outside but weak on the inside. In fact, they are cautiously proceeding step by step to test the international trend towards them. Since the publication of the Lytton Report, the entire puppet state has been terrified. At the same time, the various righteous armies are like drinking an exhilarating tonic, vying to recover lost territory. Except for the five major cities of Jilin, Changchun, Harbin, Liaoning, and Heilongjiang, everywhere else is surrounded by righteous armies. Fearing that the righteous armies would indeed make a loud declaration during the League of Nations meeting, which would be tantamount to openly providing the League of Nations with strong evidence proving that the puppet state was not established by the self-determination of the 30 million people of Manchuria, the Japanese have recently been extremely apprehensive, vigorously attacking righteous armies in various places and prohibiting newspapers outside the customs from publishing their military news to prevent leaks. In addition, they are forcing Chinese groups in various places to draft telegrams according to the main points of opposing the Lytton Investigation Report, drafted by their military police and special service agencies, and send them to Geneva via Japan. The puppet state representative, Ding Shiyuan, then compiles and submits them to Matsuoka Yosuke, the Japanese representative attending the League of Nations, for forwarding to the Council. The main points of the anti-report, which the military police deliver to each group, are as many as forty, generally stating that "Manchukuo" was established by the 30 million people suffering from the oppression of the old warlords and seeking self-determination, with the assistance of allied countries. All Japanese officials who have joined "Manchukuo" have obtained legal "Manchukuo" citizenship. The Lytton Report is biased, listens only to one side, and is too unfair. The League of Nations should organize another investigation team to come to "Manchukuo" for investigation, etc. Zhang Jinghui, Li Shaogeng, Zang Shiyi, Han Yunjie, and others have drafted one copy of this anti-report telegram each. Commercial groups draft one to three copies, and elementary school students also draft one copy per grade. Other private individuals with some reputation also draft one copy. Most of the people drafting telegrams, except for traitors, are forced and unable to escape, so they connect the various points within the designated scope and perfunctorily comply. The most ridiculous thing is that elementary school students, not even ten years old, are also forced to draft anti-report documents. Each elementary school has no choice but to have teachers write on their behalf, or have students write ten or twenty words at random and send them in. The Japanese only need to have the original copy and do not care about the skill of the writing, and they are all telegraphed to Geneva according to the original text. Perhaps this childish trick will be seen at the League of Nations meeting in the future. The Northeastern newspapers, all those run by Chinese, are now under extreme pressure. Before the League of Nations has even convened, the Japanese military police have issued a notice stating that they must not publish news other than that of the Japanese United Press, and must not carry pessimistic articles about the puppet state. The Japanese United Press provides dozens of telegrams to each newspaper every day, all of which are propaganda in nature, and each newspaper must pay to purchase them, and must publish them without omission, without selection, and especially without deletion or modification. This is truly unprecedented suppression in the world. Apart from a portion who are willing to flatter Japan and spare no effort to promote and praise the Japanese, the others are lifeless. It is expected that when the League of Nations convenes, Northeastern newspapers will have no way to find real news, and even if they obtain news, they will not dare to publish it. (November 18th)

Page 7

Manzhouli

Japanese Consul Yamazaki's Report on the Incident Diary

Since Su Bingwen's rebellion, the Manzhouli Railway Protection Army also clashed with the Japanese police force. Japanese Consul Yamazaki besieged the area, unable to escape. The Chinese and Russian consuls mediated several times, but due to the hostile actions of some Cantonese Railway Protection Army personnel among the Japanese residents, the Railway Protection Army headquarters did not allow it. The following is an abridged translation of Consul Yamazaki's diary, as reported to the Japanese government by the Tokyo Jiji Shinpo.

September 27, 10:00 AM—Received a phone call from Wu Delin, Deputy Commander of the local Railway Protection Army, inviting me and Captain Ohara and Lieutenant Yano to the headquarters for a discussion. I took Secretary Fukama and went to the headquarters with Captain Ohara in a carriage. After a strict inspection by the guards, we entered the reception room on the upper floor. Gunfire suddenly broke out inside the room and in the city. Shortly thereafter, the regular aircraft between Qiqihar and Manzhouli soared into the sky. The Chinese soldiers immediately opened fire. The aircraft, realizing the danger, immediately landed and transported Mr. Sayama, the Manchurian resident of the company, back to Qiqihar. Commander Wu was quite angry with the Railway Protection Army towards the Japanese police and stated that he had no way to suppress it, requesting that the police force be disarmed immediately. I agreed to his request, knowing that the four to five hundred soldiers of the Railway Protection Army could not be defeated by a small number of police officers. Subsequently, Captain Uno decided to exchange the protection of the lives and property of the remaining members of the team and the residents. I issued a disarming order to Captain Uno's team, which was carried by Secretary Fukama. Captain Uno had previously instructed the police force by phone, but the police force continued to fire fiercely. As a result, the Railway Protection Army returned fire, causing Secretary Fukama to be unable to advance. He turned back and asked Captain Uno to call the police force again. At that time, I also knew that if the disarming was not carried out quickly, the situation would worsen, and I immediately ordered all members to go to the battlefield to explain the advantages and disadvantages, leaving only me at the headquarters. Secretary Fukama, under the pretext of comforting the residents, was able to return to the consulate. Later, Captain Uno and Commander Wu went to the police headquarters to observe the situation of the second defense line of the Railway Protection Army. Captain Uno alone told the soldiers that they would disarm. Then, he returned to the headquarters with Captain Ohara and Commander Wu. Secretary Fukama, as previously agreed and with the permission of Commander Wu, was escorted by three soldiers to break through the defense line on the way and return to the consulate. The consulate was silent, and the doors were tightly closed. After about twenty minutes, I also returned to the consulate. Sugii, the police chief of the consulate, sent Officer Shiozaki as an escort and set off in a carriage, ordering the officer to inspect the barracks area. About twenty minutes later, I was surrounded by Chinese soldiers. At that time, there were only six officers. I gathered the staff inside a corner of the consulate to resist the invasion of the Chinese soldiers. At the same time, I ordered Secretary Matiba and Officer Nakazawa to burn the telegraph codes. On one hand, I ordered the foreign women and the families of the staff to gather inside the consulate, totaling no more than thirty-one people. However, there were only a few pistols in the consulate, making it difficult to resist. At this time, the officer who went to the front line to observe the situation reported the situation outside. Shortly thereafter, Secretary Fukama returned to the consulate and reported that the police force had been disarmed. I then realized that we had no defensive power. Matsui, the police chief, and the other six police officers had no choice but to abandon their weapons and adopt a policy of non-resistance. I also knew that the situation was urgent and urged the staff to burn the seals and confidential documents. At this time, it was difficult to connect by phone, and the consulate was heavily surrounded. Since it was impossible to move freely, I had to send a secret envoy through the back door to sneak to the Soviet consulate, asking them to negotiate with the Railway Protection Army to withdraw from Manzhouli. The Soviet consul said that he needed the permission of the Chinese government before he could prepare vehicles. I knew that withdrawal was impossible. At 5:30 PM, several officers and soldiers came to investigate the weapons inside the consulate. I handed over the nine pistols of the police officers inside the consulate. Afterwards, they inspected the weapons inside the houses of the Japanese residents. Fortunately, with the help of Chinese Officer Zhou, I went to Ichido Street to investigate and rescue the foreigners and inquired about the damage situation. Except for the residents on Sido Street and Godo Street, all were accommodated in the consulate. Officer Zhou returned to the consulate at 1:00 AM on the 28th. At that time, the Border Protection Police Force, following Captain Uno's order, disarmed all members and imprisoned them in the office of the police station. After disarming, Captain Uno went to the Railway Protection Army headquarters with Captain Ohara. At night, Officer Shiozaki did not return, and the gunfire on Sido Street and Godo Street was mixed, and the consulate was surrounded by armed soldiers, causing extreme terror. Everyone stayed up all night, suffering greatly.

28th—The staff could not go out a step. Postal and telegraph services were strictly prohibited. At 11:00 AM, Liang, a lieutenant colonel, visited and accommodated the foreigners and the families of the police force on Sido Street and Godo Street in the consulate. At 2:10 PM, a Japanese aircraft flew over the consulate. Everyone gathered in the consulate was very excited and came out of the ceiling, holding up the Japanese flag to indicate that they were safe. At 2:30 PM, I used the phone to ask the Russian consul to relay the message from Chita to Vladivostok to Ambassador Hirota, begging the foreigners to return to their country via Vladivostok. At noon, a Chinese regiment leader visited, verbally describing the movements of Ohara and Uno and offering to send them back to the consulate. However, at 3:00 PM, the commander of the Railway Protection Army suddenly telegraphed that he was unwilling to escort Captain Ohara and Captain Uno.

29th—At 10:00 AM, I borrowed 3,000 yuan from the Russian consul. The Russian consul still replied that he needed the permission of China. On the other hand, Takahashi Tomiko disguised himself as a Russian woman and was accommodated among the Russian refugees.

30th—At noon, two or three Chinese squad leaders and soldiers searched the consulate for weapons. At 4:00 PM, the Russian consul sent 3,000 yuan, entrusting him to deliver 1,000 yuan to the Hailar dispatcher. In the afternoon, to purchase food, the Civil Society dispatched a member to the market under the supervision of Chinese guards.

October 1st—At 11:00 AM, Zheng Wenfu, adjutant to the headquarters, visited and asked about the situation of Ohara and Uno. Subsequently, by order of the Railway Protection Army headquarters, he came to the consulate every day to report on the safety of Ohara and Uno. However, the Russian side said that sending money to Hailar required the consent of Su Bingwen. At 4:00 PM, Wang, Li, Chen, and other three adjutants, along with several guards, visited, saying that they had received a secret report that Japanese were hiding and resisting behind the roof of Japanese merchant Hirashima Shichisuke's house and planned to go with Secretary Fukama to inspect. They also brought Commander Wu's official document. Thus, Fukama and Shiraishi went to investigate the condition of nearby houses.

October 2nd—For days, it has been quite troublesome to purchase food. The headquarters dispatched Peng Shaojiang, adjutant to the consulate. At 10:00 AM, Adjutant Zheng came again and asked the adjutant to take out bedding and clothes from Captain Uno's house. At 4:00 PM, it was delivered as promised. At 5:00 PM, Secretary Fukama negotiated with Adjutant Zheng for the reconciliation of member Hito Hira, and requested the release of Miura Kamezo and two Koreans. (To be continued)

The Opium Ban in Shanxi Province

Taiyuan Correspondence. The formerly model province, now transformed into a den of demons, Shanxi, has seen a proliferation of narcotics in recent years. It could also be called a national model. In the central counties, such as Yuci, Taigu, Qixian, and Pingyao, traditionally known for their wealth, the sales volume of "white powder" (i.e., heroin) reaches over 300,000 taels annually (each tael valued at around sixty or seventy yuan). In the southern and southeastern regions, such as Xinjiang, Yuncheng, Jincheng, and Changzhi, "red pills" (i.e., gold pills, known as "red pills" by the Shanxi people) are widespread and can be said to be fashionable. If a stranger travels from Yuci to Changzhi or Yuncheng (the former being over 600 li away, the latter over 900 li), every small shop along the route sells white powder and red pills, allowing them to indulge their habit. Even during these times of strict prohibition, the northern counties of Yanbei, though poorer, have naturally seen a slight reduction in the influx of high-quality imported powder. However, after being occupied by the Fengtian Army outside the Yanmen Pass, tens of thousands of acres of fertile land were converted to growing opium poppies, and the production of "black goods" (opium) is likely comparable to that of neighboring Shaanxi, which previously held a monopoly on its cultivation. Over the past twenty years, China has been plagued by natural disasters, epidemics, and the ravages of soldiers and bandits. Shanxi, compared to other regions, could have been considered a paradise on earth. However, even though this paradise had not suffered from war or banditry before, the evil flames of narcotics had long since anesthetized most of the people, bringing them to the brink of death.

When the Cabinet resigned the year before last, and Shanxi banknotes ceased to be redeemable in silver, the rural economy, which had been shaken, faced complete bankruptcy. The sustenance of over a hundred thousand mercenary troops depended entirely on the burden borne by the common people. Extortion and levies appeared endlessly. Despite all efforts to extract funds, the government authorities could not resolve the financial difficulties. Consequently, the government had to find other ways to open up new sources of revenue and stop past substantial leakages. This new policy was "strict enforcement of the opium ban."

The so-called "strict enforcement of the opium ban" involves the provincial government inviting local celebrities to form a "Committee for the Investigation and Prohibition of Narcotics." Any powder or pill peddlers caught are sent to military court for trial. Regardless of the quantity sold, as long as it can be proven that they were selling, they are sentenced to death. Since the establishment of the Narcotics Prohibition Committee in October of the twentieth year of the Republic, prison carts filled with powder peddlers are commonly seen heading to Xin Nanmen to be executed by firing squad. In the past year or so, the number of those sent to their deaths has numbered in the hundreds, including several women. Naturally, we have no sympathy for these pests who harm the country and endanger the people. However, we cannot help but pity those small-time powder peddlers, most of whom only sell two or three qian, or half a tael or one tael. The truly large-scale dealers are rarely caught. Driven by family burdens and the pressures of making a living, they have no choice but to take this risk. Although the enforcement is so strict, whether the narcotics can be eradicated is another matter. The reality is exactly the opposite of the original intention. While the small-time peddlers are gradually eliminated, this creates a wonderful opportunity for the big dealers to get rich. For instance, a certain army stationed in southern Shanxi openly deals in narcotics on a large scale, taking advantage of transportation and the organization of the military. Who would dare to touch a hair on their heads? Those who are addicted cannot help but use, and those who deal cannot resist the lure of profit.

At the same time, the "Official Medicine" sold exclusively by the "Village Administration Office" of the provincial government, namely, anti-addiction pills, contains 70% opium as its raw material. The annual sales amount to about 1.5 million yuan. Because it is difficult to sell them, the government has to step up improvements in order to compete with white powder and red pills. What kind of improvements? The result is a new type of pure raw paste called "Anti-Addiction Medicine Cakes." These cakes are made from opium. How is this raw material obtained? After the war in Yanbei, all the fertile land outside the pass was used to grow opium poppies. When the Fengtian Army withdrew, the harvest was purchased by the Shanxi provincial government. There was talk of lifting the opium ban last year, but it was halted after opposition from the public. Since May of this year, about two thousand boxes of anti-addiction medicine cakes (each box weighing fifteen kilograms, i.e., twenty-four jin) have been sent out by post offices every month. We cannot but admire the sincerity of our government in banning opium. Is it because too few people are seeking treatment? In August of this year, a large number of opium prohibition commissioners were specially appointed and stationed in various counties to implement the ban and exclusively promote the sale of official medicine. In addition to a salary of thirty yuan each commissioner can earn a commission of ten percent on the sale of official medicine. Thus, a large number of commissioner bosses, full of authority, have taken office.

"Strict enforcement of the opium ban" means that both white and black goods are forbidden for sale, but official medicine is an exception. Doesn't the government realize that the people of Shanxi's addiction will only deepen? The intangible losses and monetary consumption are insignificant compared to the loss of physical strength, which is a real loss to the nation. It is hoped that the authorities will pay attention to this. (November 21st)

Xiong Bin Returns to Beijing After Finishing His Work

The Situation of Liu's Troops Being Transferred and the Issue of Downsizing

Jinan Correspondence. Xiong Bin, the Chief of the General Affairs Department of the General Staff Headquarters, went from Jinan to Laiyang on the 18th of this month to oversee the transfer and departure of Liu Zhennian's troops. He left Laiyang on the 23rd, went to Qingdao via Weixian, and met with Naval Commander Shen Honglie. On the evening of the 25th, he took the Jiaoji train west from Qingdao and arrived in Jinan this morning (the 26th) at 7:00 a.m. Governor of Shandong Province Han Fuju, Civil Affairs Director Li Shuchun, Mayor of Jinan Wen Chenglie, and Chief of the Public Works Bureau Tu Kairu, among others, all went to welcome him. After alighting from the train, Xiong went to the Jiaoji Hotel with Han and others to rest. According to what Xiong told reporters, the results of his trip to Laiyang were satisfactory. Currently, in Laiyang, only two regiments of instructors and special agents remain; in Laizhou, only one independent brigade and the division headquarters remain. When he left Laiyang on the 23rd, the division headquarters had already set out. The military department dispatched a total of twelve transport ships to Yantai. The second brigade of Liu's troops filled five ships, which had already set sail on the 23rd and are expected to arrive at their destination today. The remaining seven ships can load the artillery regiment, cavalry regiment, engineer regiment, and logistics battalion that are heading to Yantai. The ships need four days to travel from Yantai to Wenzhou, one day for upstream rest, and another four days to return from Wenzhou to Yantai, for a total of ten days round trip. Since the military department ordered Liu's division to depart as soon as it arrives, without waiting in Yantai, they have to wait for the ships to return before departing. It is estimated that they will be able to completely depart Shandong in another three weeks. As for the downsizing issue, the central government originally intended to complete it before the transfer, but the military department's order was issued on the 17th, and the troops in Laiyang had already set out on the 17th, so there was not enough time. Therefore, it is hoped that the downsizing will be done after arriving at the new defense area. I also suggested that it should not be done in too much of a hurry. A mutiny occurred in a part of Liu's troops in Laiyang on the 24th, which was due to the anxiety caused by the news of the downsizing. I am eager to return to Beijing not only because the mission of overseeing the troop withdrawal has been completed, but also because I urgently want to report this matter to the central government. After arriving in Beijing, I plan to first meet with Minister He to report, and then telegraph Chairman Chiang for instructions. Whether to go to Wuhan or not will depend on Chairman Chiang's reply. When Liu's troops first arrived in Laiyang to defend the city, the order was quite chaotic, but it has recently improved. The departure was indeed without much disturbance. I have instructed them to release the vehicles that were requisitioned after they arrive in Yantai, and they have agreed. They are very satisfied with the central government's arrangements. The people of Laiyang suffered greatly this time. During the siege, some starved to death, some threw themselves into wells, and on one occasion, a group of refugees who had just left the city were caught in a misunderstanding and shot, resulting in many deaths. It is very distressing. The damage to the houses in the city is still small, mostly in the west and south gates, which were demolished by Liu's army to clear the line of sight. Liu claims that his troops suffered few casualties. In short, what I am most concerned about is the issue of downsizing, because Yantai and Longkou have a mix of Chinese and foreigners, so it must be done carefully to avoid accidents. Downsizing in Zhejiang would be more appropriate. I will report this idea to the central government, and so on. At 9:30, Xiong boarded the Pingpu southbound train back to Beijing. Han Fuju and other important figures all went to the station to see him off. (November 26th)

Planning the Construction of a Major Northern Port

The Preparatory Committee Has Been Established

Zhang Hanying Hired as Chief Engineer

Jinan Correspondence. Preparations for a major northern port have now begun. The Preparatory Committee has now invited Zhang Hanying, the Chief of the Higher Education Section of the Shandong Education Department, to be the Chief Engineer. (Zhang is the current president of the Shandong Engineering Society and formerly an engineer at Huludao.) After being hired, Zhang has resigned from his position as section chief in the department. This evening (the 24th) at 6:40, he took the Pingpu Train 202 from Jinan to Tianjin. According to people in engineering circles, the location of the major northern port is in Leting County, between the Daqing River and the Can River. The terrain is suitable. This place is suitable not only because it was designated by Sun Yat-sen, but also because it is actually the best harbor in northern China. Five li from the coast, the water is thirty feet deep, allowing very large ships to dock. Compared to Huludao, Huludao has more mountains, so the water is deeper, making port construction easier, but building city houses is more difficult. This place has no mountains, making port construction more difficult, but building city houses is very easy. China's only good northern port, Qinhuangdao, is not under our sovereignty. The painstaking efforts of twenty years in Huludao were also abandoned halfway, which is very disheartening. At this time, building a major northern port is essential. Once the construction is successful, the prosperity will definitely be above that of Tianjin. It can become the only port for North China, Rehe, Chahar, and Suiyuan Mongolia. Products can be exported from here. This year, Suiyuan produced a surplus of wheat, and some was even burned. If this port is established, it can be transported and sold from here.

Page 8

From this, the importance of this port is self-evident. Both the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways are paying close attention to it. An office has been set up near the Wei River, and the Preparatory Office is located in Tianjin. There are currently two engineers stationed there to measure tides, and climate, record rainfall, test the strata, and produce a 1/10,000 scale map to carry out various preparations for port construction, and measure the Gu Tai station feeder line. Roughly, the preparation and design will take about five years. The project cost is estimated at fifty or sixty million yuan. As for how many years it will take to complete, it is still difficult to predict at this time. The Preparatory Committee has a total of five members. The chairman of the committee is Li Shutian, and the engineer is Zhang Hanying. Below them are engineers. (November 24th)

Zhang Xueliang Hosts the Beiping Press

Report on the Trip South

Yesterday (the 24th) at 3:00 p.m., Zhang Xueliang met with the Beiping press at the Shuncheng Wang Mansion. More than fifty reporters attended. They were first received by Shen Nengyi and others, and then Mr. Zhang appeared and reported on his recent trip south. The reporters also raised eight questions: (1) The situation of meeting Chiang and Soong in Wuhan; (2) Japanese propaganda claims that Zhang's trip to Hangzhou was related to national defense issues, what is the truth; (3) Whether he will attend the Third Plenary Session, and whether he has any proposals; (4) Is it true that the antiques of the Forbidden City will be moved to Luoyang for safekeeping, and what are Zhang's opinions on the preservation of antiques; (5) There are many rumors about Feng Yuxiang, what is the truth; (6) The recent situation of bandit suppression in the three provinces and the pursuit of the Xu Xiangqian and He Long factions; (7) The progress of the Su Ma situation in Heilongjiang Province; (8) The situation on the border of Rehe. Mr. Zhang answered them one by one, as detailed below.

Reasons for going to Wuhan and Hangzhou: The reasons for my trip to Wuhan were no more than the following three points: (1) Regarding the military and political affairs of the North, I had not met with Chairman Chiang for a long time to discuss them. In addition, the Military Branch Council has been reorganized and established, and I am the acting chairman, so I went to Wuhan to report and fulfill my personal responsibilities; (2) Chairman Chiang originally planned to come to the North to meet with me. I thought that Chiang was planning the suppression of bandits in Wuhan, and the affairs were important, so I went to meet him and asked Chiang not to come; (3) I met with Minister Soong to discuss the finances of the North. Everyone knows that the finances of the North are difficult. When I visited Soong, I discussed whether there were other ways to solve the problem. You are asking me today, and I think this is also the reason. I met with Chairman Chiang twice during my trip to Wuhan. Minister Soong returned to Shanghai in a hurry to handle the affairs of the China Merchants Bureau. Before leaving, he asked me to go to Hangzhou to continue the discussion. I originally planned to go with him, but I rested for a while, so Soong went first, and I flew to Hangzhou the next day to meet with Soong and continue to discuss financial issues. At the same time, I also visited the Aviation School. Although I did not completely finish the discussion with Minister Soong, the general results were already achieved. Soong returned to Shanghai first, and I also left Hangzhou to return to Wuhan, where I bid farewell to Chiang and returned north. The rumors that I went to Hangzhou were related to national defense are purely unfounded. Why would national defense affairs be discussed in Hangzhou? In fact, Minister Soong returned to Shanghai because of the China Merchants Bureau issue, and he had not had time to discuss it in detail in Wuhan, so he asked me to continue the meeting in Hangzhou. Minister Luo also asked me to meet in Nanjing, but I declined because I was anxious to return to the North.

The issue of the antiques of the Forbidden City: The Third Plenary Session is about to open, and whether I will go to Nanjing to attend will depend on the situation. I am not prepared at the moment. I am a supervisory member, and it doesn't matter whether I attend or not. I have no proposals for the conference. After Supervisory Committee members Gao and Zhou arrived in Beiping, I have not met with them. I will not express any opinions on this issue. I have only seen the news about moving the antiques to Luoyang, and I don't know the details.

Rumors about Feng are unfounded: There are many rumors about Mr. Feng Yuxiang. As far as I know, Mr. Feng is unfairly treated. Mr. Feng likes to talk, which is a sign that he is not indifferent to the country. He cannot but speak. I am very confident that Mr. Feng has no other actions. The rumors are not credible. Song Mingxuan (Zhe Yuan) resigned from his position as chairman of the Chahar Provincial Government is another matter and has nothing to do with this.

The situation of bandit suppression in the three provinces: Regarding the situation of bandit suppression in the three provinces, I met with Chief of Staff Cao Haosen of the General Headquarters in Wuhan. According to him, the bandit suppression is being carried out in two directions, south and north of the Yangtze River. At present, only two factions remain in the north, Xu Xiangqian and He Long. He Long's troops have only three thousand people left and are powerless. Xu's troops have more than ten thousand people, and there are more guns than people. The pursuing troops found many branches of juniper on the backs of the horses left behind by Xu's troops, which can be used as proof. At present, all parties are paying close attention to Xu's troops. Xu was a student at Whampoa Military Academy and had worked in political work in Shaanxi. This time, he pasted slogans along the way, calling for "Opening up the international route." The goal is probably the Shaanxi-Gansu area. Chairman Chiang has ordered troops to thoroughly pursue and suppress them, which will not be difficult to solve. In any case, we cannot allow Xu's troops to sneak into Shaanxi, otherwise, it will not only be difficult to solve, but also affect the security of the North. I met with Zhang Fang, who is in charge of post-war rehabilitation in southern Henan. What he has seen and heard must be the truth. Regarding the brutal behavior of the Communists in southern Henan, he has taken many photos. One photo shows the heads of people killed by the Communists, piled up with no less than several thousand, including the heads of infants, which can be described as extremely tragic. Zhang also personally saw places marked as "killing fields" in every county he visited, with as many as seven or eight in each place. It is conceivable how violent they were. I have also heard about the tragic murder of Yue Weijun by the Communists. It is said that Yue was hung up and beaten once a day after being captured. Sometimes, when Yue's relatives and friends sent money, he would be treated better for a few days. But when the government troops advanced to suppress the bandits the previous month, the bandits were unable to resist and prepared to retreat. Before retreating, they planned to subject Yue to the cruel punishment of skinning him alive. The method was to cut a slit in his neck with a knife and rub it with alcohol to peel off the skin while he was still alive and not dead. Yue knew that he could not escape, so he asked to give a speech before he died, and said that he would not make any opposing remarks. So the bandits gathered a meeting, and Yue went on stage and spoke at length about the crimes of the Communists. Before he could finish, he was chopped twice by the bandits. His right hand, because he was wearing a jade bracelet, was also chopped off. The situation was very tragic. The bandits originally planned to throw his body into the water, but someone in the bandits suggested that Yue's relatives would definitely prepare money to redeem the body, so they preserved his body. Later, the bandit suppression army suddenly arrived, and the bandits abandoned Yue's body and fled in a panic. I heard that after Zhang Huizan was killed, his body was thrown into the water. It can be said to be tragic. As for the names of the Communists' killings, they are also extremely diverse. One type is called the "dissatisfaction" crime, and the most people are killed. If the bandit leader sees that a person's expression is slightly unhappy when talking to him, he will be driven to be killed. Hearing this kind of thing is really sad. But internal strife also arises within the Communists from time to time, and they kill each other. Several famous Communists in Henan have also been killed. Female Communists are called "Party Aunts," which is extremely ridiculous. The Communists use them to mobilize the army, making it easier to approach and engage in agitation. I asked if these people were willing to be Communists. It is said that most of them are coerced. The Communists are most severely killing the intellectual class, and leaving behind fools to be used as tools. This matter is of great importance to the future of China. At present, young people think that China has no way out and are trying to use the Communist Party's claims as an experiment, but they do not know that they are going down a wrong path. The Communists also train children in the bandit areas. A certain army captured a member of the Communist Party named Zhou, who was only ten years old. When interrogated, he was threatened with the death penalty, but he was not afraid at all and said, "I am not afraid of death." From this, we can see that the Communists are paying such careful attention to elementary school children. In addition, the recovered bandit areas all have arsenals, hospitals, factories, etc., everything that should be there.

The situation on the border of Rehe is complicated: The recent telegrams from Ma Zhanshan and Su Bingwen in Heilongjiang Province have been selectively published. In the future, they will continue to be released as necessary. The situation on the border of Rehe is extremely complicated. There are no special circumstances at this time.

Guangdong Issues 4 Million in New Paper Money

Preparing to Issue a Second Phase of 10 Million in Aviation Bonds

Guangzhou Correspondence. Recently, since Guangdong Province banned the export of silver, the exchange rate has risen sharply, especially the Hong Kong dollar exchange rate, which has risen to over 44. Foreign trade is declining, and stores in various industries, with winter approaching and a great need for cash, are in a state of credit crunch. In order to regulate the market, the Provincial Bank plans to issue another 4 million yuan in provincial fractional notes, which was submitted to the Provincial Council yesterday (the 22nd) and approved for record. In addition, the military authorities, in order to expand the air force, previously issued 5 million yuan in patriotic aviation bonds, which were distributed to various parties for promotion and sales. Since the issue, only 800,000 yuan has been sold. A lottery was held once before. However, a mere 800,000 yuan is far from the original issue amount. Therefore, it is planned to issue a second aviation bond to quickly raise large sums to expand the air force fleet. On the 18th of this month, a special meeting was convened by four institutions, including the 1st Army Group Headquarters, the Air Force Headquarters, the Department of Finance, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, to discuss the second issuance method and amount. As a result, it was decided to issue another 10 million yuan. The issuance procedures and lottery methods are roughly the same as the previous regulations, but the difference is that the promotion and sales procedures have been changed to quota sales. The amount to be allocated to each county is specified, and they are required to complete the sales and submit the money within a limited time. The issuance time is planned to be divided into three periods, with four months as one period. 3 million yuan is sold in quotas each period, and they are required to complete sales within one year. The first period is from December 15th of this year to April 14th of next year; the second period is from April 15th of next year to August 15th; the third period is from August 15th of next year to December 14th. It is heard that after this quota sales method is decided by a special meeting, it will be submitted to the Southwest Political Affairs Conference for approval and implementation. (November 23rd)

Guangdong Army Consolidates Defense of Southern Jiangxi

Order to Loyal Citizens to Relocate to Suppress Local Communists in Southern Xiongzhou

Bandit Traces Discovered in Western Jiangxi, Coordinate with Hunan Army to Suppress

Guangzhou Correspondence. Recently, the Communists in southern and western Jiangxi are plotting to become active again. After the return of the commander of the 1st Army, Yu Hanmou, to defend, the Guangdong Army actively deployed defenses. The Ganzhou Xingying issued a notice a few days ago, advising the people in the area of southern Jiangxi to store food in advance, and dividing the residents into A, B, C, and D household registration. A and B households should purchase three months of food, C households one and a half months of food, and D households one month of food, and ordered all households to complete the storage between a certain time. For the sake of supervision, the military headquarters implemented the dispatch of personnel for inspection and sealing. Recently, the Independent 3rd Division dispatched the 3rd Regiment to search and suppress local Communists in the Youshan and Zhangling areas within Southern Xiongzhou. But many of the loyal citizens were still living there. When the bandit was being suppressed, there was a fear of a difficult separation of good and bad. The regimental headquarters then convened a local meeting to implement the relocation of loyal citizens in order to suppress bandits. The Youshan Zhangling area's villages, such as the twenty-six villages in the Zhenping township, the forty-seven villages in the Datang township, the eleven villages in the Qiaodu township, the seven materials of the Daojing township, the fourteen villages of the Pingitan township, all of them should be relocated to another area before November 22, and all food should be moved as well in order to prevent aiding the bandits. As for Ganzhou, according to recent news, there are about 2,000 more Communists in Xingguo, and bandits are also gathered in Ban Jing and Xingren, seemingly moving to Wan'an, attempting to assist the Communists in western Jiangxi. Commander Yu Hanmou, according to reports, is in contact with Chen Cheng's division of the Central Army in Wan'an to maintain vigilance, and ordered the regiments of Ye Zhao's division of his department to tighten the defense of Ganzhou, build blockhouses, and install electric nets. And sent the 6th regiment of Ye's division to Jin Tang and other places to tighten the defenses. On the first division's side, Deputy Division Commander Mo Xide is directing his troops to set up defenses in the Tanbang area at Shangyu, and working with the Hunan Army to search and suppress Kong Hechong's faction of the pseudo 7th division of Communists in western Jiangxi. The Hunan militia had previously repelled the Kong bandits who invaded Baitutan in Liling, eastern Hunan. The remaining bandits have scattered and fled to the remote areas of western Jiangxi. Therefore, in order to prevent bandit troubles, the Guangdong Army has ordered the 3rd air squadron stationed in Shaozhou to send aircraft to reconnaissance in the western Jiangxi area for days. But on the 15th, they discovered red flags in the mountains and valleys, and the Communists were moving westward in single file, seemingly heading towards eastern Hunan. They immediately flew back to report. Commander Yu immediately telegraphed Wang Dongyuan's division of the Hunan Army in eastern Hunan to quickly send troops to Yingqian and arrange to cooperate in the suppression, so that nothing is missed. (November 19)

Reasons for Economic Decline in Northern Anhui

Social Unrest Due to Soldiers and Bandits

Rural Bankruptcy After the Flood

Commercial Recession and Financial Stagnation

Report from Bengbu: Amidst the national economic decline and business depression, northern Anhui has suffered economic ruin, hardship for the people, and growing social unrest due to years of communist banditry and last year's floods. This is unprecedented in decades. The reasons are complex, and the significant points are analyzed as follows: ① Military Impact: In terms of transportation, northern Anhui has convenient land routes through the Jinpu Railway and waterways via the Huai, Fei, and Ying Rivers. Geographically, it controls Jiangsu and Shandong to the north and connects Henan and Hubei to the west. Any conflict makes it a battleground for military strategists. Over the years, northern Anhui has invariably been affected by wars. Undisciplined troops, wherever they go, arbitrarily requisition supplies and exploit the people relentlessly, severely damaging the people's vitality and repeatedly hindering the social economy. ② Banditry Impact: The people of northern Anhui are inherently tough. In recent years, due to frequent wars, the docile have been subjected to oppression, while the cunning have taken risks. Unscrupulous individuals have seized the opportunity to rise up, and with the Communist Party taking the opportunity to incite, the power of bandits and communists has grown rampant day by day, committing arson, murder, rape, and pillage, leaving no evil undone. The people in bandit-controlled areas have suffered immensely, with fields lying barren, homes in ruins, and economic hardship beyond description. ③ Natural Disaster Impact: Northern Anhui is located in the Huai River basin, where most residents are farmers, producing a variety of grains. Last year, unfortunately, a major flood occurred, turning twenty-one counties into a watery expanse, exacerbated by hailstorms, which devastated agricultural products. The rural economy was completely bankrupt, leading to a lack of purchasing power, farmers crying out in distress, and a daily increase in unemployment. ④ Impact of Taxes: Northern Anhui is relatively far from the provincial capital, and some remote counties are almost isolated. Feudal forces are extremely powerful, making it difficult for the provincial government to intervene effectively. As a result, corrupt officials collude with local tyrants and evil gentry to engage in harmful activities, leading to a proliferation of various exorbitant taxes. The collection of boat taxes along the upper and lower reaches of the Huai River is particularly onerous. Recently, a grain permit fee has also been levied. The government's exploitation leaves the people with no means to complain. Farmers, burdened with heavy taxes, have no choice but to sell their harvested grain at distress prices, resulting in a situation where cheap grain hurts the farmers. ⑤ Impact of Money: Northern Anhui has suffered from natural disasters and human-caused calamities for years, causing the nascent industry and commerce to plummet. After the depression, it has continued to decline. With the people lacking purchasing power, there is a significant shortage of cash. Major banks in Bengbu, due to the difficulty in recovering loans, have stopped lending, leading to tight credit, financial stagnation, and increasingly difficult cash flow. Shop closures are frequently reported. (25th day)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang

The County Government Convenes a Winter Defense Meeting: The County Government believes that in the current winter defense period, local security should be planned for in advance. Therefore, yesterday (27th), it convened the 21st Annual Winter Defense Meeting. Attendees included officers from the land and water police forces, the head of the security bureau, and leaders from various districts. County Magistrate Shen Yong chaired the meeting, and the following matters were discussed: ① Adoption of the Winter Defense Outline; ① Whether there is a need to redeploy land and water police forces during the winter defense period should be comprehensively planned by the land and water police forces and reported to the county for record; ① During the winter defense period, the passwords for the police whistles and military garrison areas may use the passwords issued by the Security Office; ① The Director of the Public Security Bureau should request the addition of winter defense police during the winter defense period to strengthen forces, and it was decided to add personnel as in previous winter defense cases, with each district adding as appropriate; ① The First District Leader proposed that during the winter defense period, for the sake of communication, the Construction Bureau should be ordered to actively install telephones to facilitate defense, and it was resolved that the County Magistrate and the Construction Bureau would jointly work with the First District Office to actively install telephones in the near future.

Bank Robbery Suspects to Be Brought Back for Trial: The case of the robbery of the Songjiang branch of the Xingye Bank, in which bandits were involved, had been without leads for a long time. Recently, Lu Ying, the captain of the Criminal Investigation Team of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, discovered the trail of the bandits in the case and led detectives, with official documents, to the relevant police station to arrest Niu Jinpu and six others. According to the confessions of Niu Jinpu and others, the case was reported to the Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for review. The suspects arrested were Niu Jinpu, Zheng Shaobo, Li Yinghan, Sun Hanquan, Niu Langshi, and Shao, all from Hefei County, Anhui Province. Niu had previously served in the military and is highly suspected of being involved in the Xingye Bank case. The government has dispatched personnel to Shanghai to escort them back to the county for interrogation and handling.

Taicang

Several Hundred Disaster Victims Go to the County to Petition: The local Relief Association distributed relief funds to various districts on the 21st, having previously sent letters to the County Government and various township chiefs, instructing them to investigate and report on the households affected by the disaster in detail for verification and distribution. However, most of the township chiefs failed to handle the matter impartially, so most of the disaster victims did not receive relief, while those who were not affected by the disaster received one or several relief tickets. This aroused resentment. Yesterday afternoon, more than 500 disaster victims gathered and went to the County Government to petition, demanding relief and requesting punishment for the township chiefs who were acting in a corrupt and biased manner. Qian, the Section Chief of the First Section, and Wu Chengzhe, an official, came out to meet them and promised to investigate and handle the matter. The disaster victims were satisfied and dispersed.

Suzhou

The Boat Accident Case is Brought to Public Prosecution: Regarding the tragic case of the overturning of a steamship at the Ancient Relics Museum of Baosheng Temple in Jiaozhi, which resulted in the drowning deaths of Zhu Liangren, Zhu Tianle, and Fu Yuwen, has been reported in this newspaper. It is now known that the steamship driver, Fei A'da, and the mechanic, Zhu A'you, were apprehended by the Third District of the Water Police and transferred to the District Prosecutor's Office. After repeated interrogations by Prosecutor Qian, the case has been concluded. Yesterday, they were indicted for causing death due to negligence in their duties. The families of the deceased have been provided with condolence money through the initiation of Zhang Taiyan, Li Genyuan, and others.

Wuxian Business Community Changes to Using Standard Measures: The County Chamber of Commerce has been ordered to promote the new system of weights and measures and is actively carrying out the task. Yesterday (26th), the committee decided that implementing both weights and measures simultaneously would be quite difficult. It was decided to start with measuring instruments first, and Shi Junqing, Shen Shuzhang, Zhu Jingbo, Yan Chuqing, and Fan Junzhuan were appointed to handle the matter. It is expected that by the first day of the lunar new year, the entire county will be using the new system.

Preparing for the Suzhou-Jiaxing Long-Distance Bus Route: The Suzhou-Jiaxing Highway, which runs from Suzhou through Wujiang to Jiaxing, has been under construction for several months since its groundbreaking. The roadbed has long been completed, and the paving of cinder pavement is currently underway. It is expected to be completed within two months. It is reported that some people have initiated the organization of the Suzhou-Jiaxing Road Long-Distance Bus Company, with an authorized capital of 100,000 yuan, divided into 1,000 shares, each share worth 100 yuan. Fundraising is currently underway, and registration is in progress.

Rickshaw Pullers Cause Trouble at the Train Station: Every time trains arrive or depart from Suzhou Railway Station, rickshaws and cars solicit passengers, causing disorderly conditions. Cui Shaobo, the new section chief of the Third Division of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Police Department, took office a week ago and immediately planned to rectify the situation. He ordered the police to confine rickshaw pullers within the boundaries of the train platform and instructed coachmen to sit on their carriages and not to get off to solicit customers. For rickshaws without licenses, a small photo identification card must be donated to the station. Those who violate the rules and solicit passengers will be severely punished. As a result, yesterday (26th) at 11:00 AM, when the Shanghai express train arrived, rickshaws and carriages responded in unison, leaving the train station and going on strike, refusing to pull passengers. They also blocked vehicles from other stations from entering the station at key intersections. Female passengers and those carrying luggage were in a particularly difficult situation. The turmoil remained unresolved by evening.

Changshu

Murderer in Fushan Case Imprisoned: Wei Fulin, a farmer from Beibaoli, Fushan District, was discovered by Su Baosheng and others while committing theft at Su's house. Su, together with Ni Tiantian and Luo Xing, chased Wei to Haicheng and beat him to death. The next morning, the town chief, together with the Public Security Bureau, detained Su Baosheng and four others and sent them to the county. According to the confessions of Su Baosheng, Luo Kangsheng, Luo Jinhai, and Xu Er, Wei was beaten by Ni Tiantian and Luo Xing, who were on the run, and they were only chasing behind them and did not lay a hand on him. As a result, the official ordered the imprisonment of Su and four others until Ni and Luo, who were on the run, are arrested, and the case will be handled accordingly. The body of Wei Fulin was taken back by his family for burial.

Dispute over Sand Fields in Shazhou: Disputes over sand fields have occurred in Shazhou City for many years, and there has been no peace. This summer, Huang Zhulou, from Shazhou Hunghu, kidnapped Lu Lianshi, the custodian of the district office, in order to seize the sand fields. Fortunately, the military and police worked hard to capture him and rescue Lu Lianshi from danger. Huang Zhulou was arrested and imprisoned, and the case has not yet been closed. Unexpectedly, yesterday (25th), Cao Yinnian, the chairman of the Sand Field Custody Committee, was supervising workers who were repairing the embankment when suddenly Sha Zaitang, a member of Huang Zhulou's gang, led a crowd of more than 200 people to seize the field. The two sides started arguing, and as a result, Sha Zaitang ordered the abduction of four laborers: Li Wanglang and Zhang Zhichang. Cao was lucky to escape and immediately reported to the district office and the Public Security Bureau, requesting the police to rescue them and urgently telegramming the County Government to inform all subordinates to find a way to rescue them. Cao Yinnian also formally filed a lawsuit with the County Government. As of the evening of the 26th, the whereabouts of the four abducted people were still unknown.

Rugao

Strange News of a Fetus Dying with a Retracted Head: Xue Zhanhu's second daughter-in-law, a resident of Xuejiazhuang, Chemahu District, Rugao, was pregnant for a full term and gave birth to a strange child on the night of the 23rd. The child initially cried, but when the midwife held it in her hands, she saw the child's head gradually shortening. In a moment, the child's entire head was inside its body, like a turtle retracting its head into its shell. It looked like a headless child. After about half an hour, the child's head still did not extend out, and it died due to suffocation. The whole village was shocked and rushed to see the strange news. It is recorded here for the study of physiologists.

Two Notorious Bandits from Xixiang Executed: Xia Zuchun and Zhu Ha, two notorious bandits from Xixiang, had committed numerous crimes over the years in the Pingchao, Baipu, and Liuqiao districts, including arson, robbery, and murder. The Land Bureau Will Be Established Soon: The Nantong County Government has been ordered to prepare for the establishment of a Land Bureau, and plans are already in place. Pig Tax Will Be Collected at the Village Level: Lou Fumin, a commissioner of the Finance Department, is responsible for collecting the pig tax in the Jiangbei counties of Tong, Rugao, Hai'an, Jingjiang, and Taixing. Since pig traders are scattered throughout the countryside, taxes will be collected uniformly at each village, at a rate of 10 per thousand.

Zhenjiang

A Military Officer Commits Suicide in Zhenjiang: Wan Chao, courtesy name Jiaoquan, a native of Shouxian County, Anhui Province, was 42 years old. He had previously studied in England and participated in the European War. After returning to China, he graduated from the First Infantry Class of the Huangpu Military Academy's Chaozhou Branch. He served as a platoon leader, company commander, and battalion commander in the Second Division of the Army and as the commander of the Fifth Battalion of the Central Military Academy's Transport Corps. In January of this year, the Independent Brigade of the Second Division was downsized, and Wan lost his job. This autumn, he came to Zhenjiang to seek a position from Chairman Gu, waiting for three months without success. After being stranded for a long time, he ran out of money. While in Zhenjiang, he had a romantic relationship with a woman, but recently he suddenly lost her. Overwhelmed by poverty and illness, he conceived the idea of suicide. On the night of the 25th of this month, he secretly went to the side of the lecture hall in Baoxian Park and hanged himself from a locust tree. On the morning of the 26th, someone discovered him and immediately reported it to the Fifth Sub-bureau of the Public Security Bureau. The chief of the bureau found three suicide notes, one to Chairman Gu, one to Director Zhou, and one to a friend, along with more than a dozen letters of appointment, party certificates, and membership cards from the Huangpu Military Academy. Director Zhou, in addition to reporting the verification, also followed Chairman Gu's order to advance 100 yuan for the coffin. Here is his letter to Chairman Gu: Honored Three Seats, Jianjun: I, Wan Chao, after graduating from the military school, participated in the Northern Expedition from Guangdong, following you, sir, and have been treated with care. However, I am ashamed of having made no contribution and have lost my job. In these nine months, I have deeply felt the difficulties of life and the monotony of life. Added to this is the memory of the past, the various ways in which I have failed people and myself over the past thirty years. Overwhelmed with pain and anger, I have no choice but to end it all with suicide. There are unspeakable secrets that I cannot tell directly. I hope you will remember our old friendship and my current plight and resolve all matters related to my aftermath. I will be eternally grateful in the afterlife.
