Pan Wanqing Crushed to Death by Car

Doctor Said Injuries Were Light

Died at Home

Pan Wang, an Anhui woman residing at No. 8, Lane 17, Haichao Temple Road, South City, is 36 years old and has a son named Wanqing, 14 years old. At around 8:00 PM the night before, Wanqing was playing at the intersection of Lujiabang when a freight car suddenly came speeding and knocked Wanqing down before he could avoid it. The wheels rolled over his abdomen, causing him to faint from his injuries. The driver, seeing that he had caused an accident, immediately sped away. Fortunately, the police officer Di Zhaorong from the local police station arrived and recorded the license plate number of the car, Third 418, and sent Wanqing to Nanyang Hospital at Xiaonanmen for treatment. After a brief examination by the doctor, it was said that the injuries were light and there was no danger to his life. At that time, his mother, Pan Wang, also arrived after hearing the news and took Wanqing home. Unexpectedly, at around 6:00 AM the next morning, Wanqing died of his injuries. In her grief, Pan Wang reported the situation to the Third Section of the First District. Police Chief Jin immediately dispatched Police Officer Zhang Hongxun to bring the car owner, Liu Ziqiao, and the driver, Zhou Zhihong, to the police station for preliminary interrogation based on the license plate number Third 418. According to Liu Ziqiao, 47 years old, from Tongzhou, he owns freight car No. 3418 of the Liu Ziji Motor Vehicle Company at No. 77 Kangti Road in the French Concession. The day before, the machine was damaged and was being repaired at a certain car shop in Lujiabang. Last night, because the car had been repaired, he ordered the driver Zhou Zhihong to drive the car back. He did not know anything else. When questioned, Zhou Zhihong, 27 years old, from Yancheng, stated that he is a driver for the Liu Ziji Motor Vehicle Company. Last night, he was ordered by the owner to go to Lujiabang to drive the car back. Unexpectedly, Pan Wanqing was lying behind the car. When the car passed near Haichao Temple, the child accidentally lost his grip and fell to the ground. He does not know anything else. Given that the child fell from behind the car, how could the wheels have rolled over his body? This is obviously a cunning excuse to shirk responsibility. As the matter concerns human life, he was ordered to prepare a document and send him to the bureau for interrogation. On one hand, the 23rd police station was dispatched to report to the Shanghai Local Court for an inquest. At around 4:00 PM, Prosecutor Yang, who was appointed by the court, arrived at the scene for an inquest and determined that the deceased, Pan Wanqing, had died of injuries sustained during his lifetime. The body was handed over to his family for coffin preparation and burial.

Robbery at Native Goods Store

The Yuanda Gong Native Goods Store at Bei Fujian Road, north of Laozha Bridge in the Public Concession, was settling accounts at around 8:00 PM last night when three robbers suddenly arrived. Two held pistols, and one stood guard in front of the door. The two robbers jumped into the store, drew their pistols, and threatened them not to make a sound. They forcibly seized the cash on the counter, totaling 48 yuan, as well as coins. They went out and fled north. At that time, someone was getting married at a restaurant across from the store, holding a banquet for guests. The robbers dared to commit robbery in a busy city. The store staff did not dare to pursue the robbers because they had pistols. They reported the incident to the police station afterward, requesting an arrest.

Two People Died Tragically

A Young Woman from Jiangbei Dies from Opium. Wang Chen, a young woman from Jiangbei, 26 years old, lived upstairs at the Laoyuan Tai Hotel on Bei Chujia Qiao, French Concession. The night before, she had an argument with her aunt and, in a moment of despair, secretly took opium and committed suicide. She was later discovered and sent to Renji Hospital for treatment but died at around 4:00 AM yesterday morning.

A Car Crushes a Gold Star Hardware Store Apprentice to Death. Liu Xincai, a 17-year-old apprentice from Ningbo at the Gold Star Hardware Store at the intersection of North Sichuan Road and Shigaota Road, was riding a bicycle out to pick up goods at around 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon. As he was traveling through the intersection of North Sichuan Road and Haining Road, a public bus, license plate number 15060, was coming from the front. Unable to avoid it in time, he was knocked to the ground and his skull was crushed, resulting in instant death. The police arrived after hearing the news, recorded the license plate number, and then sent the body to Tongren Hospital by car and then to the coroner's office to await examination.

Fire at Wan'an Street

At 4:50 PM yesterday afternoon, a fire broke out at the Minsheng Industrial Raw Materials Factory at No. 10 Wan'an Street in the city. Zhu Shilin, a guard from the First Branch of the Second District, immediately reported the incident to the police station by telephone and notified the fire brigade. Section Chief Shen also dispatched Police Officer Ma Yumin with policemen to the scene to maintain order. When the fire brigade's pumpers arrived, they tried their best to extinguish the fire. However, the fire was very fierce, and the firewood of Zhao Xiangshan, the sub-tenant of No. 8, was piled next to the chimney of the Minsheng Factory, causing the fire to spread very violently. After all the fire engines arrived, the fire was finally extinguished. It is estimated that the Minsheng Industrial Raw Materials Factory at No. 10 was completely destroyed, and the fire also spread to the neighboring Nos. 8, 6, 12, and 16 (only half of No. 16 was destroyed), totaling more than ten houses destroyed. After the incident, the arsonist had already fled. Only Liu Azhuang, a 14-year-old apprentice from Hangzhou at the Minsheng Factory, Ren Jianzhi, 19 years old, a rickshaw puller with the surname Zhu, and Yao Xiuquan, 44 years old, a tenant of No. 8, were detained and brought to the police station. After interrogation by Section Chief Shen, Ren Jianzhi stated that he pulls a rickshaw for Song Ligong, a former district officer of the Fourth District in No. 10. Today, in the evening, the chimney of the material preparation stove inside the Minsheng Industrial Raw Materials Factory, where I live, was burning day and night and was very fierce. The firewood of the sub-tenant of No. 8 was piled inside. I was working outside. When I went back today, I saw a fire on the way, so I came together. Section Chief Shen verified the statement and, as Wu Fushi, the sub-tenant of the Minsheng Factory, was at large, it was decided to further investigate whether there was any arson and then verify the matter.

Formerly Used by the General Volunteer Corps

Confiscated by the Police and Ordered Confiscated

Chen Ruhai, a Chinese detective of the Huishan Police Station, learned that the Huaxingchang Machine Factory at No. 607 Maohai Road was privately hiding military firearms. He reported this to the police chief, who obtained Search Warrant No. 5072 from the First Special Court. At 10:45 AM the other day, Chief Detective Walter of the Western District and Detective Chen went to search the factory and seized 45 fake rifles and 47 bayonets. These fake weapons were exceptionally well-made, with mechanisms and appearance almost identical to real guns. The only difference was that they could not be loaded and fired. According to the factory's responsible personnel, these fake guns were custom-made by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce School for use in training the volunteer corps. Later, the school did not accept the goods because the style differed from the original design, so they were left in the factory. Since the detectives determined that the items were not real guns, they did not arrest anyone, but took the fake guns and bayonets back to the police station. They were then sent to the summary court of the First Special District Court. The police lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, requested the court to decide how to dispose of these guns and knives. Chief Detective of the Western District submitted a report on the circumstances of the search and seizure, and Magistrate Huang Risheng reviewed the report and ordered all items seized to be confiscated according to the list.

Ministry of Education Promulgates

Kindergarten and Elementary School Curriculum Standards (8)

Chinese Language

First, Objectives

1. To guide children in practicing the use of the national language and develop their accurate listening and speaking skills.

2. To guide children in learning simple vernacular language and appreciating children's literature, to cultivate their reading ability and interest.

3. To guide children in practicing composition to develop their ability to express their feelings and ideas.

4. To guide children in practicing handwriting to develop their accurate and swift writing skills.

Second, Types of Assignments

(1) Speaking

(i) Listening and speaking in daily conversations. (ii) Practice in delivering speeches, debates, reports, and storytelling.

(Note) Standard Mandarin should be used in teaching this assignment to facilitate communication across the country. If there is a shortage of teachers who can use Standard Mandarin, oral teaching should be done as closely as possible to Standard Mandarin.

(2) Reading

(i) Intensive Reading: Select appropriate teaching materials to guide children in reading carefully and in detail, enabling them to appreciate and understand, or to memorize through understanding, emphasizing quality. (ii) Extensive Reading: Select appropriate teaching materials or supplementary readings, set a time limit, guide children in reading, and then have the teachers examine them separately and discuss them with the children, emphasizing quantity.

(3) Composition

(i) Utilize the environment to design activities that allow children to narrate or write to practice description, argumentation, and expression of ideas. (ii) Enable children to understand and use the format, structure, grammar, rhetoric, and punctuation of ordinary practical writing.

(4) Writing

(i) Practice: Practice regular script and cursive script at fixed times, and design practical letters, announcements, etc. for practice. (ii) Recognition: Recognize the running script, cursive script, and simplified forms of commonly used characters.

Third, Main Task Items for Each Grade Level

Grades 1-2 Weekly Time Grades 3-4 Weekly Time Grades 5-6 Weekly Time

1. Describe what you see.

2. Practice using everyday language.

3. Practice with organized language materials.

4. Be able to engage in easy and interesting daily conversations.

5. Practice telling stories, etc.

Notes

1. The teaching materials for the reading section should focus on children's literature, supplemented by ordinary and practical writing with literary qualities.

2. Time allocation is calculated based on direct teacher guidance in class.

3. Speaking, reading, composition, and writing should be taught together in the first and second grades.

4. From the third and fourth grades, speaking, reading, composition, and writing can be taught together or separately. If taught separately, they should be connected.

5. Important historical and geographical materials should be added to ordinary and practical writing and poems.

Ministry of Education Promulgates Second Table of Curriculum for Senior and Junior High Schools

Four Differences from the Previous Curriculum

The Ministry of Education yesterday issued an order to the education bureaus of all provinces and cities, stating: "The Table of Subjects and Credits for General Science Courses for Junior and Senior High Schools was previously promulgated and implemented by the Ministry in August and October of the 18th year of the Republic, along with the Provisional Standards for Curriculum. In August of this year, the Ministry held a revision conference for the curriculum standards of senior and junior high schools, and formulated the Table of Teaching and Self-Study Hours per Week for Each Subject in Each Semester of Senior and Junior High Schools, which was approved by the conference. This Table of Hours is significantly different from the previous Provisional Standards in terms of subjects and credits. (1) Because secondary education is still based on the academic year system, and teaching of each subject is still calculated by time, the credit system is abolished to avoid confusion in calculating credits and teaching time. (2) Junior high school extends the basic training of elementary school, and senior high school cultivates a good foundation for entering university. All subjects and time have been carefully reviewed and recorded, without adding a burden on students. Therefore, compulsory subjects are abolished in both senior and junior high schools. (3) In accordance with the central resolution, Party Principles teaching materials should be incorporated into subjects such as Civics, History, and Geography, and no longer be set up as a separate subject of Party Principles. (4) Stipulating self-study hours allows for the proper allocation of students' total daily learning time, to achieve a balance between work and rest, and not hinder physical and mental development. In addition, the Second Table of Teaching and Self-Study Hours per Week for Each Subject in Each Semester of Senior and Junior High Schools was formulated, adding Mongolian, Hui, Tibetan, and second foreign languages to accommodate the special needs of various regions. The above two tables have been reviewed and corrected by the Ministry and are promulgated by ministerial order. The table is hereby attached, twenty copies each. Please instruct all subordinate middle schools to follow them uniformly from the next semester. This order is hereby issued."

Second Table of Teaching and Self-Study Hours per Week for Each Subject in Each Semester of Senior High School

Semester First Grade Second Grade Third Grade

Total Hours

(Explanation) (1) This curriculum table only applies to the senior high school department of complete middle schools established in special areas that require Mongolian, Hui, Tibetan, or a second foreign language. (2) The second foreign language refers to Russian, German, French, Japanese, etc. (3) In special circumstances, if necessary, the Ministry of Education may be requested to waive the English course and replace it with one of the second foreign languages. (4) The total daily hours of class, self-study, and extracurricular exercise for senior high school students are stipulated to be ten hours, calculated as sixty station hours per week. (5) In addition to class time, one hour per day is for morning exercises and extracurricular activities, and the rest is for self-study. (6) Teachers must supervise and guide during extracurricular exercise and self-study time. (7) Senior high schools that use this curriculum table must first submit a request to the competent educational administration authority and forward it to the Ministry of Education for approval and record-keeping. (8) Senior high schools that use this table may reduce English by one or two hours per week if they encounter special difficulties, but they must submit a request to the competent educational administration authority and forward it to the Ministry of Education for record-keeping.

Unprecedented Football Showdown at the Baseball Field

Shanghai China and Hong Kong Intercity Teams

First half ended zero to zero, second half ended one to one.

| Evenly Matched, Wonderful Performance |

| Audience of Over 18,000 People |

The result of yesterday's battle between the Shanghai China football team and the Hong Kong Intercity football team was a tie, with each team scoring one goal. Both sides played cautiously, and there were many wonderful moments. The situation was slightly better for China than Hong Kong, but the shots were difficult to score. The first half ended zero to zero. In the last quarter of an hour, each team scored once. The audience was packed, like Yiyuan, with about 18,000 people, setting a new record for the baseball field. Mayor Wu Tiecheng performed the opening kick-off ceremony. Western football clubs and the National Sports Association will host banquets tonight and tomorrow night. Some of the players will travel south on Wednesday.

Mayor's Ceremonial Kick-Off

Numerous Chinese and foreign guests and spectators graced the occasion, attracting considerable attention. Mayor Wu Tiecheng, accompanied by his young son, Youliang, made a spirited appearance on the field for the ceremonial kick-off. Seizing the opportune moment, Shen Siliang requested the Mayor to perform the honors for this grand match. With a powerful kick by the Mayor, the fierce competition began.

China vs. Hong Kong Lineups

Chinese Team:

Liang Shutang, Chen Zhenhe

Lan Ning, Chen Hongguang

Zhou Xianyan, Feng Yunyou, Li Yichen

Jiang Shanjing, Chen Jiaqiu

Tu Kaiyuan, Chen Yutian

Hong Kong Team:

Charlie Bradley

Lau Mau, Sun Chung-shun

Roger Pado, Thomas Mullen (Above), Wong Mei-shun, Mullen (Below), Wai

Pado (Below), Wong Mei-shun (Above), Leung Wing-chiu, Cheng Siu-leung

First Half: 0-0

Jiang Shanjing Repels the Enemy

As three o'clock approached, the heroes of both teams entered the field in an orderly fashion. After a brief warm-up, the silver whistle blew, and after the Mayor's kick, the battle commenced. The southern team aggressively advanced northwards. Bradley took the lead, with Pado providing central support, and Bradley launched an attack on the western flank, breaking through the central defense line and heading straight for the Chinese goal. Jiang Shanjing roared, rushing out to intercept. Li Yichen then led his forces in a counter-attack.

The Brave Li Ning Defends Against Two Armies

Chen Hongguang initiated an uprising on the eastern outskirts, with Xiao Heitan (Little Black Coal) not wanting to be outdone, launching a fierce offensive directly into the heavy defense. Lau Mau, not wanting to appear weak, launched a diagonal attack, overcoming difficulties. Cheng Siu-hong unleashed his forces on the eastern flank. Tu Kaiyuan, unable to stop them, faced an extremely critical situation as the wolves entered the house. Li Ning, with his formidable spirit, arrived in time. Zheng, realizing the gravity of the situation, made a short pass to Wong Mei-shun, but before he could take several steps, the pass was intercepted by Li Ning and passed forward.

Leung Wing-chiu's Lone Rescue

The ball seemed to be bewitched, darting east and west, disregarding the defensive lines. Feng Yunyou and Huo Wei competed in a 50-meter sprint. Ju Kaiyuan intercepted the ball skillfully, passing it to Xiao Heitan, who advanced, relentlessly penetrating the defense like a violent storm. Hongguang, Yichen, and other generals had already approached the city. Lau Mau and Mullen met the enemy separately, but they were outnumbered. Luo Gun was like a fish in a pot, helpless. Leung Wing-chiu, increasingly frustrated, returned to the defensive line and, finding an opportunity, launched a shot, clearing the danger and temporarily bringing calm to the Hong Kong goal.

Zhou Xianyan Dribbles Like a Lion

Under Huo Wei's command, a major counter-attack was launched. Bradley was as cunning as a hare. Although Jiang Shanjing was happy to respect the player but not the ball, the ball dropped low. Feng Yunyou caught up to snatch it, but Bradley had already passed it to the center. Li Ning and Mei-shun jumped up simultaneously, but neither made contact. Sun, with his iron legs, was lying in ambush on the side, sweeping the ball away from the goal. Zheng Siu-hong and Huo, quick as lightning, had already reached the front of the goal. Zhou Xianyan leaped up, seized the ball, and sent it out of danger, dribbling like a lion, earning thunderous applause.

Cheng Siu-hong, Like a Tiger in a Cage

Sometimes to the south, sometimes to the north, the game changed constantly. Although the Chinese forwards were brave, the Hong Kong goalkeeper's great improvement made it difficult to score. The Hong Kong team's wing attacks were also anticipated by the Chinese defense. Cheng Siu-hong was closely guarded by Liang Shutang, like a tiger in a cage, unable to unleash his power, making it difficult for the Hong Kong team to gain an advantage.

0-0: No Progress Made

Chen Jiaqiu dribbled the ball into enemy territory, with Chen Yutian supporting him on the side. Li Yichen aided the attack, dribbling past Pado. Leung Wing-chiu skillfully used a back pass. Tu Kaiyuan sat firmly at the boundary line, strictly inspecting for spies. Xiao Heitan and Chen Hongguang echoed each other, sending the ball back and forth. Ma Lun soared into the air. The ball returned to the center of the field, where both teams continued their efforts. However, time was not on their side, and the "lemon time" (end of the half) had arrived, with both sides scoreless.

Shanghai Chinese Football Team Photo (Li Zunyong)

Second Half: 1-1

Both Sides Maintain a Tense Stalemate

The athletes from both teams took a short rest, revitalizing their spirits. After switching sides, they resumed the battle, with both sides creating dangerous situations. For 35 minutes, neither team was able to break the deadlock. Xiao Heitan frequently scratched his head, and the 21,000 spectators were both startled and amused, not knowing whether to laugh or cry. The situation was tense and difficult to break.

Hong Kong Team Adjusts Defense to Cope with the Critical Situation

The Hong Kong team's defense was under pressure, with frequent warning signs. The key defender, Mullen, had suffered an injury in the first half. To strengthen the defense, they reorganized their line, with Pado retreating to the rear to replace Mullen. Wong Mei-shun returned to her forte in the central defense, guarding the interior and supporting all sides. Huo remained in the interior, while Zhou Lun took on the role of midfielder.

Fierce Battle Between Two Armies: Chen Jiaqiu Jumps to Head the Ball (Li Zunxi)

Close But No Cigar: What a Pity

The Chinese team's repeated attacks all ended in vain. Although the opportunities were good, they were unable to capitalize. Twenty minutes into the second half, Chen Zhenhe charged straight in from the left, advancing through several lines and reaching the warning zone. The divine soldiers were linked together, and there was no one at the Hong Kong goal. Heitan considered passing to the center, which would have been incredibly advantageous and easy to score. However, the central forward, Li, arrived and fumbled the opportunity. Chen Jiaqiu also watched it slip away. By the time Yutian regained possession, the enemy was already prepared. Unable to penetrate the goal, what a pity.

Jiaqiu's Header Leads to Fall of Hong Kong City

With only twelve minutes remaining in regulation time, Feng Yunyou took a free kick from 40 yards away from the enemy goal. The ball came back and forth, and he shot three times. The ball swirled around for a while. Li Yichen, blocked by Lau Mau, quickly passed to Heitan. Lau Mau rushed over to intercept again, but Heitan dodged and launched a powerful kick, sending the ball to the center. The right winger was waiting for the opportunity to strike. Chen Jiaqiu saw the ball coming and, at just the right moment, bent down and headed the ball. Boom! It hit the mark! The first goal was scored!

Mullen, Though Injured, The Iron Gate is Breached

The victory was already in the hands of the Chinese team. Hats flew into the air, and cheers erupted. It would have been difficult for the Hong Kong team to launch a sneak attack. In the next five minutes, the Hong Kong team put all its efforts into a counter-attack. Wong Mei-shun sent a pass to the center, and the injured general Mullen dribbled the ball straight up, breaking through the midfield line and reaching the front of the goal. While Zhou at the iron gate was stunned, Ma Mao launched a high ball, which went into the corner of the goal. The misunderstanding of offside resulted in a draw. After that, Heitan had one fierce shot, but it hit the wooden corner of the goal instead of going into the net. In a split second, the whistle blew, signaling a draw.

Victory, Defeat, and the Situation

Both Sides Were Cautious in Defense

Both sides were wary of the opponents' fierce attacks, so they were extremely cautious in defense. It was rare to see the central defenders rushing forward to push the attack, as they were focused on preventing the enemy forwards from maneuvering. Therefore, only the forwards of both sides were seen advancing and retreating, creating this kind of situation. The Chinese team paid particularly close attention to closely guarding both wings. This was the reason why it was difficult for both teams to make progress.

The Performance Was Extremely Exciting

Because both sides were very careful in their play, and wary of making mistakes, the whole game was exciting to watch. The Hong Kong goalkeeper and defenders were all excellent. On the Chinese team, Jiang Shanjing was particularly energetic. Zhou Xianmen and Li Ning also regained their original form. Among the forwards, Chen Yutian missed some opportunities in the first half, and Chen Hongguang did not perform particularly well, missing his shots several times.

Local News

Meeting of the Commanders of the Local Boy Scout Troops

Opposing the Puppet Regime Sending Boy Scouts to Japan

Initiating Donations to Help Refugees in Northeast China

The Shanghai Boy Scout Council held its tenth city-wide meeting of Boy Scout troop commanders at 4:00 p.m. yesterday at the headquarters of Troop 196 of the Liangjiang Women's Sports School on Fangxie Road. Zhu Jiarang from the Municipal Party Headquarters attended to provide guidance. Troop commanders Wang Gang, Xie Yanbo, Zhou Mingshi, Luo Lie, Gu Qingxiang, Qu Yue, Feng Zhenwei, Chen Guangzhen, Jiang Yinhui, Huang Shan, Xu Jingtang, Shen Yu, Yu Julu, Huang Shengbai, Wu Yiqiu, Liu Yucai, Wang Dongqi, Hua Mingsheng, Cao Yuncheng, Leng Xueqiao, Yu Liaoyuan, Fan Xi, and more than 30 others attended. The meeting was chaired by Wang Gang, recorded by Xie Yanbo, and proceeded as usual. First, the chairman reported on: 1) fundraising for the Chinese Boy Scout Air Force Plan; 2) the preparation status of the Nanjing headquarters; 3) the registration situation; and 4) measures to commemorate the four Boy Scouts who died while serving on the battlefield. The following discussions then took place: 1) Troop 196 proposed a plan to regulate uniforms, and it was resolved to hand it over to the council. The measures are as follows: A) The council will crack down on anyone with untidy uniforms at intersections or public places; B) Regarding the color of scarves, the council will collect samples from each troop and announce them; C) Boy Scouts who use ties instead of scarves will also be cracked down on. 2) Troop 230 proposed that military bands should use unified teaching materials, and it was resolved to hand it over to the council. 3) Troop 270 proposed that the council should hire specialist coaches for assessment purposes, and it was resolved to hand it over to the council. 4) Troop 268 proposed that the selection of troop commanders should be subject to strict ten-level scrutiny, and it was resolved to hand it over to the council for submission to the headquarters. 5) Troop 383 proposed that if troops in the city are disbanded, their seals and certificates should be taken back by the higher authorities, and it was resolved to hand it over to the council. 6) Troop 270 proposed that the dispatch of Boy Scouts by the puppet regime to Japan for pro-Japanese activities should be uniformly opposed, and it was resolved to ask the council to submit it to the headquarters for review. 7) Troop 121 proposed raising donations to help refugees in Northeast China, and it was resolved to hand it over to the council.

Free Talk

Max Xiang Bo's Sayings on Zhu Xi's "Feet"

— Jing Ji

Old Man Xiang talked about... decades ago, when he traveled to Xiamen, he personally saw that the women in that area kept their heels an inch or two off the ground, which was very strange. When he asked about it... the local gentry replied very formally... this was Zhu Xi's "feet," and they did not dare to change the ancient legacy! He then asked why Zhu Xi would care about this and design these "feet"? At that time, someone replied, in a scholarly tone... "To prevent lewdness!"

I talked about Wang Yangming's experimental method of teaching students to investigate things, which involved having them sit and observe a bamboo shoot growing for several days. Now, let's talk about Zhu Xi saying that lewdness cannot be prevented without feet, so he designed a set of rules that made movement difficult. One called for investigating things until you get a headache; the other prevented lewdness by restricting feet!

In fact, self-restraint is the key to becoming a sage; it is not about this or that! Please read on!

"What does lewdness look like? It is like water flowing out of a river... At first, one's face is still red with shame, but soon the mind is completely lost! Animals often point the way, and the gods watch the dark boudoir; it is better to be diligent in self-restraint, for chastity is a golden embankment."

This is a poem by Mo Jing titled "Chastity Restrains Lewdness." The Western sage, Erwo Lue, said: "Thinking deeply about the image of death and burial can best prevent evil thoughts!" This is a story from the Middle Ages!

"Once there was a monk who saw a beautiful woman dressed neatly; later, the image of her was always in his mind! Not long after, the beautiful woman died of illness and was buried before she was embalmed; foul water flowed everywhere; the monk saw this scene, soaked a handkerchief in the foul water, and kept it. Whenever evil thoughts were about to arise, he would smell the handkerchief and say to himself, 'The beautiful woman I saw the other day has reached this stage today!'"

The Book of Han records... When Lady Li was about to die, she did not want to see Emperor Wu of Han... Emperor Wu of Han only thought of her, and then he became suspicious!

Anda's Four Anti-Japanese Heroes

— Nankong

After the three northeastern provinces were occupied by the Japanese army, the people, unable to bear the Japanese army's trampling, rose up in resistance against Japan. Volunteer armies sprang up like mushrooms, each seeking the survival of the nation. The Japanese army found it difficult to cope and was exhausted, resulting in unprecedented chaos in the three northeastern provinces. Volunteer armies in various places repeatedly captured cities. The ferocity of the resistance war was truly rare. The Anda station was particularly fierce, having been captured and lost several times. The recent capture of the Anda station by Deng Wen's troops was due to the efforts of four anti-Japanese heroes. These four heroes were also members of Deng's volunteer army. Two were brothers surnamed Mu, one surnamed Zhang, and one named Liu Yunpeng. They were daredevils in Deng's army. Before Deng attacked the Anda station, he first sent secret agents to Anda to investigate the strength of the Japanese army. At that time, the Japanese army defending Anda numbered a full regiment, part of the 11th Division that invaded Shanghai. Deng's volunteer army numbered about 800, with 500 guns. Having heard that the Japanese army in Anda wanted to attack Baiquan and were being transferred to the front line, he took this opportunity to order the selection of 50 daredevils, all carrying grenades and armed with broadswords and pistols, to serve as the vanguard and attack Anda at night. The four heroes bravely volunteered for the daredevil team and, with the others, marched quickly at night. As they approached Anda, the Japanese army had already set up sentries in a village three miles from the station. The volunteer army moved forward like snakes and were spotted by the Japanese army, who shouted the password. The Zhang surnamed soldier leaped up and fired his pistol, and a Japanese soldier fell in response. The Japanese army behind them, hearing the sound, quickly sprayed gunfire. The Mu brothers, disregarding their own safety, threw grenades, and with a loud boom, smoke filled the air, killing many Japanese soldiers. Liu Yunpeng, behind them, shouted and waved his broadsword forward, killing a Japanese soldier. The Mu brothers and Zhang followed, and the crowd swarmed forward, directly attacking the Japanese formation. Deng immediately supervised his troops to advance. The Japanese army was greatly shocked and quickly sprayed machine gun fire. Zhang was hit in the arm, and blood poured down like a waterfall, but he ignored it.

Research on Waste Utilization

— Yue Min

Using newspapers to wrap things is not necessarily a way to utilize waste, but using it to wrap food seems wrong. I have seen that in the food stores along North Sichuan Road, especially those opened by Cantonese, almost nine out of ten use newspapers instead of wrapping paper for food items such as cakes, candies, snacks, marinated foods, and preserved meats. One day, I bought a bag of sponge cakes and, upon opening it, smelled a strong kerosene odor that made me want to vomit. It was also stained with black spots. In the end, I had no choice but to throw it into the trash because the ink on newspapers is made of a mixture of ink and kerosene. Leaving aside the fact that it's unappetizing, even if you force yourself to eat it, aren't you afraid of harming your health? I think that those who are responsible for local hygiene should strictly ban this practice.

Wielding his blade in fierce combat, Liu rolled forward on the ground with Zhang until they were only six or seven steps away from the machine gun. Liu threw a grenade at the Japanese army, and Zhang immediately tried to seize the machine gun with one arm, but unfortunately, he was shot in the chest by the Japanese army and died. The Mu brothers also pounced to Zhang's aid and seized the machine gun. The surprised Japanese army retreated, and the volunteer army shouted and pursued them, taking advantage of the momentum to capture the Anda station. Without the extraordinary courage of these four heroes, the success or failure of the entire operation would have been uncertain.

Artification | Civilized Citizens Love Art |

— Bi

Now everything has to be "artified." Building houses has to be three-dimensional and "artified." Arranging rooms has to be simple and "artified." Tailoring clothes has to be fitted and "artified." Drawing advertisements has to be eye-catching and "artified." Shaping eyebrows has to be curved and "artified." Women's walking has to be swaying and "artified." Speaking has to be elegant and "artified." Writing has to be humorous and "artified." It is said that the civilization and barbarity of a country can be judged by whether its citizens love art. Anything that takes art as a prerequisite is considered a first-class civilized country.

It's not difficult. Let's try to "artify" everything. When eating, move your chopsticks rhythmically and continuously between the bowl and your mouth, preferably displaying the appearance of a wolf devouring its prey. This great behavior is "artified." If a husband and wife are at odds, don't just scold and cry; instead, use wooden sticks and kitchen knives to beat each other. Only when you've cracked heads, shed blood, and staggered back and forth is it "artified." Roads should not be paved flat, because that's too monotonous. They should be paved with high and low sections, so that cars bump up and down like electric chairs, and that can be considered "artified." Public and private clocks should be "artified." They should not all be the same; some should be fast and some should be slow, all different. Open-air pit latrines should be set up along the streets, and they should all be of different styles. That can also be considered "artified." Don't just shoot people; change to hanging. The facial expressions of the criminals after death, with their eyes wide and tongues sticking out, are most "artified." Don't cut your hair when it grows long, don't wash your face in the morning, don't brush your teeth, take a few puffs of opium, hunch your shoulders high, say a few words, and yawn. That can be completely "artified." When scolding someone, first roll up your sleeves, slap your thighs hard with both hands, then touch your fingers to the other person's face, and let saliva fly over their head. That is "artified" scolding.

If everything is "artified," perhaps we can also hold our heads high and be great citizens of a first-class civilized country.

Last Week's Gold Market Advances

Increase···Twenty-Three Taels Strong

New High Prices Are Constantly Emerging

Last week, the gold market's benchmark price experienced a prominent peak, with agile movements and frequent new records. Although there were no excessive disturbances, international news was turbulent, saying that the U.S. debt problem was brewing uncertainly, causing the gold market to be stormy and unpredictable, changing rapidly. The state of disarray was particularly unstoppable, with daily differences of five or six taels. In general, the exchange rate continued to fall without any end in sight, causing the Shanghai market to be greatly stimulated and prosperous, breaking through the 780 tael mark. The short sellers were severely hit and rushed to increase their positions. From the beginning of the week, the price rose and then fell again. The silver market, exchange rates, cotton, etc., all fell together. The opening was high, at 760 taels and 8 qian, an increase of 2 taels and 1 qian. Shortly after, foreign news mentioned a U.S. proposal for gold and silver protection, which dampened people's spirits, and finally the price reached 56 taels and 1 qian. Although the silver market did not fluctuate the next day, yesterday's expectations for a long position were not fulfilled. Exchange rates continued to fall, and there were rumors that the United States did not express sympathy and that war debts were postponed. Therefore, there were still many buyers, and the price briefly rose to the 60 tael mark. However, later, because the Central Bank swapped a large amount of forward exchange with the Cantonese banks (5,600 contracts), only advancing 6 taels, the market price was only calculated at 56 taels and 7 qian. However, bills of exchange were still good, and eventually increased by more than 5 taels. On Wednesday morning, the situation was the opposite of the 10th. Large contracts that looked short actually went long, so the opening was low. It was then reported that Italy had paid off a war debt of £1.4 million, and the price quickly broke through 60 taels again. Yarn and Cotton

Last Week the Yarn Market Showed

Continuous Decline

丨Spot Sales are Equivalent to Despair 丨

The cotton yarn market has been weak and depressed for a week, but the decline has not been too sharp due to floor price concerns. Although the environment is harsh, new sellers are wary. However, the market is shrinking step by step, and demand is extremely sluggish. All parties have no intention of purchasing, mainly due to financial exhaustion and the ongoing civil war, which has led to a decline in commerce. As a result, yarn sales are considered hopeless, and northern cotton yarn continues to arrive in Shanghai for competitive sales, which has led to an increase in the inventories of various factories. The daily sales volume is at most between 500 and 600 bales. Under these circumstances, how can the yarn market be sustained? Most people are psychologically inclined to sell short and watch the decline. Although the long positions of the Wing On Factory are struggling hard, the trend is such that the downward trend cannot be reversed. They have slightly reduced their long positions midway, so the price has recently broken through the 40 tael mark. Currently, due to the difficulty in obtaining cotton and the shortage of supplies, the market is relatively firm. Yarn used for cotton towels and bedding has less sales. The future situation is not optimistic. The total purchases by various gangs for the entire week were only 2,085 bales. The market price has fallen by about 1 tael. Standard yarn has recently fallen by 1 tael, while Liaoning yarn has risen by 0.25 tael. The total transaction volume for the entire week was 153,450 bales. Last Week the Cotton Market Was Relatively Stable

丨Not Assimilated by the Downturn in the World Cotton Industry 丨

Due to Scarcity and Depleted Spot Supplies

Although the cotton market has been extremely high-spirited for a week, it is naturally possible to decline in this downturn in the world cotton industry. In addition to the manufacturer’s vigorous sale of 200,000 bales, this amount accounts for three-quarters of the market, and the force can be described as strong. However, the market is still difficult to fall, because farmers in all directions are unwilling to sell cheaply, and the number of supplies from various sources is small, resulting in the Shanghai money stores having weakly low storage. As for the American market, it has fallen back to 5.78 points, but the shrinking US exchange rates makes it difficult to calculate for those purchasing to sell silver. The Indian market is also the same. The supplies that arrived successively last month have little accumulated in storage, so there is this reason. Merchants still maintain a slow, quiet, and steady attitude. In short, there is too little spot, resulting in a tight cotton and weak yarn situation. According to the Indian market report, the situation is good, and if Indian cotton purchases can go smoothly in the future, this local cotton may have a drastic change, otherwise it will be difficult for general cotton to decline greatly. According to the source on the dock, there are 2,072 bales of Yao cotton and 12,793 bales of short cotton. The total transaction volume of standard cotton for the whole week was 442,800 bales. The price of standard cotton for each month fell by 5 fen to 1 qian compared to the previous week, and the price of American cotton fell by 25 pounds. The Crossroads of Death ㈡㈩㈦

— Fan Yanqiao

Gengsheng naturally agreed and followed her into the elevator to room 436. He had no time to examine the room's furnishings at this point, eager to hear her story. There was no need to dwell on matters of love either, as he suspected something important was about to happen.

Ai wrung her hands, raised her face, and said, "Oh heavens! How is it that I still see you?" Gengsheng said, "I saw you in the elevator during the day, but I didn't dare ask because I was so bewildered by your fashionable appearance at the time that I couldn't firmly believe it was you." Ai clapped her hands and said, "That's right! I thought so too. I saw two small holes under your left ear. That's your mark, your unique feature. People from Jiangbei and other places often have their ears pierced at the behest of their parents and wear earrings, which is very, very common. But I know that back then, one hole wasn't pierced through, so they pierced a second one, resulting in two holes existing side by side. That's unique to you."

"Ah! So, you were looking closely at me, not at my name tag."

"Spare the small talk. I have something important to discuss with you."

"What is it?"

"These past few days, I've been pestered to death by someone, and this person is my enemy. It's ridiculous that he doesn't recognize me, and he's courting me. I think simply rejecting him would be too easy on him. Is there a good way to deal with him?"

"Who is it?"

"It's Han Muliang, who used 'one hundred and fifty dollars' to buy your lifelong companion!"

"Hmm..."

"Originally, I didn't recognize him because he used to be a minor official in the XX department, and he had a small mustache. Also, he's so haggard and much thinner than before. Later, he revealed his real name to me and told a big lie, saying, 'I'm not married yet.'"

Gengsheng chuckled. Aili also laughed and said, "He even boasted to me about the sincerity and exclusivity of his love, saying he drove away a concubine who hadn't done anything wrong. And that's supposed to be sincere and exclusive? Men are truly experts at lying!"

"He would never have imagined that the woman he now loves is the same one he previously rejected." Gengsheng rested his elbows on his knees, supporting his chin with his hands, looking up slightly, staring directly at Aili. Aili offered him a cigarette, but Gengsheng shook his head. Aili lit one for herself, putting it in a very thin and long cigarette holder, the cigarette and holder together measuring a full six inches. She pursed her lips, compressing the tobacco into a thin line, and slowly, artistically, blew out the smoke. Gengsheng felt like he was in a movie theater, watching a Hollywood female star performing. He couldn't help but say, "No wonder that thief is confused and can't recognize you. Even I, if I didn't notice the mole on your left forehead, wouldn't have the slightest suspicion. Look at yourself in the mirror. Where is the image of the former Aigu?" Aili said, "Indeed! I've become a different person. Honestly, I've become one of the most despicable and dangerous women in society. I'm even thinking of doing something even more dangerous to teach a lesson to those so-called young masters who only use banknotes to buy flesh." After saying this, she angrily threw the half-smoked cigarette out the window, not caring what was outside. She was extremely indignant and didn't care about anything. Gengsheng, at a loss, couldn't think of the right words to comfort or dissuade her. He could only force a smile, nod, sigh, and try to soothe her with a mix of responses.

Later, Aili asked Gengsheng how he became a soldier. Gengsheng said, "What's there to say about being a soldier who fights against our own people? Now we're fighting against foreigners, but I'm still not willing to do it. There's really no food to eat, and I'm not willing to be a bandit, so I'm forced down this path." Aili raised her thumb and said, "This time, your XX Route Army's more than twenty days of hard fighting can be compared to 'Qi Jiguang fighting the Eastern Barbarians.'"

Gengsheng couldn't help but laugh and said, "Have you seen that play?" Aili nodded, and after a brief silence of three minutes, she suddenly stood up, sat down next to Gengsheng, turned her head, and asked, "Do you need money? My heart is willing to give it to you, but my body is no longer able to."

"Of course."

"Don't misunderstand! You might think I'm a dancing star, so I can't give it to you. Think about the past few years. You used to walk under the chastity arch in our Cuiwei Village. Then you'll understand it's 'cannot,' not 'unwilling.'"

"So, what are you planning to do?"

Aili brought her mouth close to Gengsheng's ear and spoke for a long, long time. This reunion scene came to a close.

Finance

Interbank Rate Drops, Call Loan Rate Rises, Market Consolidates

Copper Coins Suddenly Exceed 4000 Cash per Dollar Again

Foreign Exchange Quiet, Taels Weak

Yesterday's market was weak due to the routine weekly bank holiday, which traditionally subdues activity in the financial and trading sectors. The interbank rate, which had recently been strong due to exports, suddenly eased. The market interbank rate was 7 yuan 1 fen 2 li 3 hao 7 hu and a half in the morning session, and 7 yuan 1 fen 2 li 7 hao and a half in the afternoon session, a slight decrease of 3 hao 7 hu and a half compared to the previous day's afternoon session. Overall, the market consolidated within a relatively narrow range. Outward remittances totaled 85,000 yuan in the morning session and only 175,000 yuan in the afternoon session, a significant drop from normal levels. Money shops cleared over 4.3 million yuan in foreign currency, while small money shops traded over 300,000 yuan.

Silver Call Loan High, No Clearing

Yesterday, no clearing occurred at the banks, resulting in quiet silver tael inflows and outflows. Silver liquidity has been tight for some time. Although rates tightened slightly yesterday, ample funds are expected to be released later, suggesting that the tightening trend will likely continue. The call loan rate was 6% in both the morning and afternoon sessions, an improvement of 2% compared to the previous day. Bill trading, ledger settlements, and new transactions totaled 5.45 million yuan in the morning session and 890,000 yuan in the afternoon and Small General Assembly sessions. Money shops and silver firms cleared over 19 million yuan, a decrease of over 10 million yuan compared to previous days.

Copper Coins Exceed Milestone

Yesterday morning, Jiangnan small silver coins suddenly fell slightly by 4 li, to 6 yuan 1 fen 5 li. They rebounded by 1 li in the afternoon session, reaching 6 yuan 1 fen 6 li. Trading volume was 5,000 corners in the morning session and 3,000 corners in the afternoon session. Guangdong small silver coins were priced at 6 yuan 1 fen 4 li 2 hao and a half in the morning session and 6 yuan 1 fen 4 li 7 hao and a half in the afternoon session. Trading volume was 75,000 corners in the morning session and 25,000 corners in the afternoon session. Due to a large influx, copper coins rose again by 5,000 cash, exceeding the 400,000 cash milestone, reaching 403,000 cash. Various exchange rates were posted at tens of cash, it was said.

Zheng Xiaoxu is Old and Not Dying

— Fo

"Zheng Xiaoxu is old and not dying" - this isn't my curse, it's Puyi's wife, Rongshi, who said it. Being old and not dying doesn't necessarily make someone a thief, but Zheng Xiaoxu certainly is a thief, a traitor to the nation. Calling him old and not dying is truly fitting.

Zheng Xiaoxu, like "an old lord blowing on a clay pot," dreams of restoration, urging Puyi to become a puppet for the Japanese, defying the great disapproval of the world. As a result, Puyi says, "How can I be considered a puppet? I am a prisoner." Since Puyi's rise as a puppet, his actions have been entirely restricted, and everything is monitored by the Japanese. Even in conversation, he must be extremely cautious, not daring to offend the Japanese even slightly, or he will be invited by the monitors to "eat a big meal." This is the evil consequence created by Zheng Xiaoxu and his gang of foxes and dogs.

Now, Zheng Xiaoxu is once again fantasizing, wanting to "pimp" for Puyi, urging Puyi to take a concubine, and even a Japanese concubine. Truly, he is a shameless person who should die a quick death. Since Wenxiu left, Puyi inevitably feels somewhat lonely. Zheng seizes this opportunity to persuade Puyi to take a Japanese woman as a concubine, both to ingratiate himself with Puyi and to express goodwill toward the Japanese. It's truly a plan with two benefits. However, since Puyi became a prisoner, his every word and action has been monitored by the Japanese. Yet, the bedroom is perhaps a place where surveillance is inconvenient. While it's nominally for Puyi to take a concubine, it's effectively placing a female monitor in the room. Puyi truly has no way out.

I recall that when Puyi was young, they planned to hire a foreign nanny. The Japanese authorities, upon hearing this, immediately convened an imperial conference, recommending the daughter of a certain duke. One of the famous three traitors of the country introduced her, attaching three conditions: first, she must have freedom of movement throughout the palace; second, the term must be twenty years; and third, she must have complete secrecy over her correspondence. Therefore, our national secrets were all known to the Japanese.

Assuming that taking a concubine becomes a reality, then Puyi will be connected to Japanese women throughout his life. He will be inseparable from the nanny in the beginning and then from the Japanese concubine. This is truly Puyi's misfortune and the root of the nation's troubles.

Year-End Reflections

— Chen Baoren

Frost and snow at the edge of the world, my dreams are uneasy;

A fur coat is helpless against the cold.

The hardships of the world make poetry a poor medicine for my troubles,

And sorrow and illness keep me awake at night.

A fluttering kerchief startles the migrating geese,

Deep feelings in letters reveal the difficulties of life.

The lights of home are waiting for reunions,

Stop listening to the pipa playing intently.

How many tears do I shed for the yellow chrysanthemums?

The sound of the new washing block mingles with the autumn wind from the north.

Common Sense

Methods for Cleaning Accumulated Dirt on Utensils

— Zuo Qi

The author previously wrote an article exclusively discussing methods for removing stains on clothing. Now, I will compile and describe methods for removing accumulated dirt on utensils, to supplement the previous article's shortcomings.

(1) Accumulated Dirt on Lacquerware: Lacquerware refers to wooden objects coated with lacquer. When lacquerware has accumulated stains, use a velvet or soft cloth dipped in a mixture of equal parts ammonia water and alcohol to gently wipe it, and it will be as shiny as new. Another method is to use a slice of lemon to wipe the lacquered surface, then wash it with soap and cold water.

(2) Accumulated Dirt on Imitation Lacquerware: Imitation lacquer is also called "Western lacquer," and its scientific name is "varnish." It changes color when exposed to heat, so when imitation lacquer has stains, do not wash it with hot water. Use cold tea or milk to wipe it. Another method is to add a little vinegar to cold water, dip a soft cloth in it, and wipe it. This is also effective.

(3) Accumulated Dirt on Enamelware: You can use loofah or a hairball coated with soap to scrub it, then rinse it with clean water. Another method is to wash it with a dilute solution of vinegar and water. Another method is to brush it with turpentine, which can also clean it thoroughly.

(4) Accumulated Dirt on Pottery: Wash it with soapy water, or rub it with salt, or wipe it with fine ash mixed with vinegar, or use a cloth dipped in turpentine. When washing dishes, add a slice of lemon peel to the water to remove any fishy, oniony, or other residual odors, and to make the porcelain surface shiny.

(5) Accumulated Dirt on Glassware: First wash it with soapy water, then rinse it with clean water. If you add a little vinegar to the water, it can make the glass shiny and clear. You can use salt or ash to rub glass cups and dishes. To wash glass bottles, fill the bottle halfway with water, add tea leaves or mustard, and shake it. Then rinse it with clean water. To wipe glass windows, add ammonia water to warm water, dip a cloth in it, and wipe it. Another method is to mix lead powder with water and apply it to the glass window. When it dries, wipe it with a dry cloth. To wash smoky lampshades, add a little vinegar and salt to warm water, immerse the lampshade in it, and wait for the soot to float away. Then wipe it clean with parchment paper or other thin paper.

(6) Accumulated Dirt on Stainless Steel: For dirt and grease on stainless steel, wash it with hot soapy water, salt water, or lye, then rinse it with clean water.

(7) Accumulated Dirt on Gold: Goldware often becomes dull after prolonged use. You can use a cloth dipped in alcohol to wipe it, then use chamois leather to rub it, or use extremely fine fire-refined gold powder to rub it. All of these methods can make it look like new.

(8) Accumulated Dirt on Silver: Silverware also easily becomes dirty and cloudy after prolonged use. To refresh it, in addition to using silver polish, you can use fragrant powder to rub it, or use a cloth dipped in dilute nitric acid to wipe it. Another method is to dissolve calcium hypochlorite in water, stirring it until it dissolves, and then use a soft cloth dipped in this liquid to wipe it.

(9) Accumulated Dirt on Copper: Copperware develops green rust after prolonged use. To remove it, first place the copperware in hot soapy water and wash it, then rub it with copper polish. Another method is to place the copperware in vinegar, soak it for a day, take it out, and then rub it with tin foil ash. You can use a cloth coated with wax to wipe brassware, and then use a clean soft cloth to polish it. You can use incense ash or tile powder to polish cupronickel items. When red copper turns black, you can use ferric chloride applied to a cloth to wipe it, then wash it with lemon juice.

(10) Accumulated Dirt on Iron: For rust on ironware, use sandpaper or fine sand to rub it, or use a brick with water to grind it. After wiping it dry, apply vegetable oil to it. For grease on pots and pans, you can

Page 17

wash them with hot alkaline water or lye to remove it. After cooking fishy or meaty foods, fill the pot with water, add two spoonfuls of vinegar, and boil it to eliminate the residual fishy or meaty odor.

(11) Accumulated Dirt on Tinware: Accumulated dirt on tinware is actually tin oxide. To remove it, first place the tinware in salt water or soapy water to soak and wash it, take it out and wipe it dry, and then rub it with incense ash.

(12) For hot water bottles and other rubber products that have accumulated dirt, you can wash them with soda (i.e., sodium carbonate) water or ammonia water.

(13) For accumulated dirt on amber beads and other ornaments,

it is advisable to wash them with milk.

(14) To remove dirt on an iron, you can use the following method: place a piece of beeswax between two pieces of velvet cloth, and while the iron is hot, rub it on the velvet cloth, and the dirt will be removed immediately.

(15) To remove ink pad buildup on seals, you can use an old toothbrush, borax, or gasoline to scrub it.

(16) Washing Sponges: First, put the sponge in cold water and soak it for a moment, take it out and squeeze it dry, then put it in water with lemon juice and soak and wash it, and finally rinse it with clean water.

(17) When suede gloves get dirty, soak a velvet cloth in milk, wring it out, and wipe the gloves with it to remove the dirt. You can also purchase soap specifically for washing leather gloves from the market.

How Are the Martyrs Now?

— Na Fu

The hands of the martyrs, the lovely hands of the martyrs!

If you inadvertently saw the hand of a martyr, it would surely make your hair stand on end, your blood boil with tension, or even excite you more. Because a human hand placed in a glass bottle, displaying grayish-white skin, with the outer layer of skin turned into fish-scale-like wrinkles, a three-inch-wide hole from a bullet wound on the left side of the palm, flowing out with handfuls of grayish-black meat fibers and a clump of reddish-black bones, obviously showing signs of being severed by a knife. At the same time, the five fingers pointing high to the sky express a kind of bravery. If you suddenly saw it, it would truly make you both grieved, fearful, and excited!

It is said that this hand is a souvenir left by a martyr who died in the "January 28th Incident" last year. In addition to this hand, there is also an equally lovely foot. There are also several huge bullets, one of which can hold 200 pounds of explosives inside, weighing a total of 600 pounds. The rest of the bullets are slightly smaller.

The things mentioned above are all war trophies from the "January 28th Incident" in Shanghai last year, and they are currently displayed in the Municipal Public Education Center. When I visited these items, I felt that it was very appropriate for them to be displayed here. First, it can commemorate our past resistance achievements and express our spirit of revival. Secondly, it can allow our people to constantly experience the gifts given to us by the brutal Japanese and the lessons of past suffering.

However, the anniversary of the "January 28th Incident" is approaching. Are the sacrificed martyrs rejoicing or grieving in the underworld? Do those of us who are still alive know?

Mailed to Mother

— Wen Bing

Mother...I have not received a letter from home for three months, and your son can only hope for the peace of the whole family! Who knew that I would suddenly receive a letter from my elder brother saying that your illness has worsened, that you have not left your room for three months, and that you have not left your bed for more than a month, wailing in pain all day and unable to sleep all night? The doctors are helpless and have no remedy. Is this my elder brother's deliberate attempt to exaggerate? It truly makes your son read it with tears flowing and release it with sorrow. I don't know where the sadness comes from, and when it will end!

Your illness began last spring and has lasted for nearly two years. The doctors say that the source of the illness is excessive labor and that it is caused by a weak constitution. This is because, for sixty years, you have given birth to children, raised grandchildren, and managed household affairs, never resting for a single day. Moreover, because we, your children, are unworthy, the family fortune has declined. Father sees this and is worried and resentful, often venting his anger on you. The mental depression is especially severe! However, you have never blamed us, your children. On the contrary, you have always cherished us like the apples of your eye, granting our every request. In the past, my elder brother was tempted by the environment and indulged in gambling. He lost tens of dollars and had no way to return home. When you heard about it, you immediately gathered money and asked someone to lead him back. My third brother liked to drink alcohol, but Father would not allow it. You would always secretly give him drinks. When I first started school, every time I came home, Father only gave me a small amount of pocket money. I was afraid of his strictness and dared not ask for more. I secretly asked you, and you always gave me the full amount. If my sister-in-law was not obedient or the sisters-in-law were not harmonious, you would try to persuade them with kind words, and the matter would be resolved. Father and you were concerned that the annual income was not enough to cover our expenses, so you often scolded beggars and vagrants. But you always borrowed money to help them, and those who received the help were grateful and praised you. When Father heard about it, he would scold you again, making you unable to rest. But you always remained the same, never changing. This is all due to your loyalty and kindness! Now that your son thinks about this, I can't help but feel deeply moved, and tears fall silently!

You were born into a farming family and grew up in the countryside. You married Father at a young age and have been busy every day ever since, never having studied poetry or books. However, you have always followed the traditional moral principles of our country, serving your parents-in-law with filial piety, treating your father with respect, teaching your children with kindness, and treating others with harmony. I have never heard of you making a mistake. Only because of this, you have given little guidance on our future. However, since I have become aware of human affairs, I have deeply felt the influence of your diligence, thrift, and kindness. I know how to cultivate myself and study, and I know that human beings originally valued mutual assistance. This is not only true at home. From now on, I will certainly uphold this principle and work harder to live up to your expectations!

When I entered the world, it was at a time of political change. For more than ten years, I have been influenced by the education I have received. I also feel the disharmony between my elder brothers and sisters-in-law. Therefore, I once requested that my marriage should be based on my own choice. You heard this and agreed without any objections. This shows that you are able to see the trends and do not want to lose my heart. It also shows that you are not as stubborn as others. As a result, although I grew up in an old family, I was able to escape the pain of old marriages and have the freedom and happiness I have today.

In the spring of the seventeenth year, my grandfather died and was buried. You worked tirelessly to manage the affairs, and at that time, you were still as healthy as ever, only occasionally losing your appetite. On February 1st, I bid farewell and came to Shanghai to study. In the autumn, I fell seriously ill. You consulted fortune tellers and gods at home, sought doctors and prescriptions, and asked my elder brother to write a letter detailing everything. Although this superstition was ineffective, it also showed your deep love for your son! Last summer in June, I took leave to return home. When I arrived home, you were lying in bed. When I asked the family, they did not tell me. When I opened the curtain and looked at you, I was shocked by your emaciated appearance, as thin as wood. At that time, you still did not easily reveal the truth, because you were afraid that I would drop out of school because of it! Before I returned to Shanghai, you vaguely revealed the pain of your illness, urging me to return early. At that time, I thought that your illness had gradually improved, so I was relieved and said goodbye again. This summer in April, I returned to Changsha and went home, but I was again involved in human affairs and left after only eight days. The doctors said that the illness was difficult to cure suddenly, but it was not critical. Who knew that it would turn critical in an instant!

My elder brother's letter said, "If you can return early, there is still a chance to see each other. If the Queen Mother of the West summons her, I will telegraph you immediately." Mother, how can your son not want to return early and throw myself into your arms? But I am adrift, with only the clear breeze in my sleeves. Where can I borrow such a large amount of travel expenses? Your son can only look up to the sky and pray, waiting until the end of the year. If the Queen Mother of the West does summon her, Mother, your son can only shed tears into the Huangpu River, hoping that it can flow upstream to the banks of the Xiang River and turn into rain to fall on your grave!

Mother, people die in Shanghai every day. In the past, I was indifferent to funerals. But recently, due to the situation, I become saddened at the sight of one. Mother, your son is truly afraid of the terror of "death"!

In this era, life has no meaning, and death is inevitable since ancient times. But because you have worked hard all your life, never resting, and have not received any material enjoyment, how can this not make your son sad and cry out loud!

Your son has never served by your side like the old Laizi, inquiring after your well-being morning and night, or performed for your entertainment. Nor can I write like Bing Xin to leave a memorial. Drifting aimlessly, I am truly unable to put your heart at ease even a little! Thinking of this, I feel deeply guilty! Now, I can only sincerely pray that your years will be prolonged, giving your son one last chance to see you. Mother, my heart is broken! I can only sincerely pray!

Edge

— Yi Ping

Outside the pass, icy sky, biting wind, red blood, white blades, flesh and blood intertwined; the mournful sound of the Hu Jia, the long neighs of warhorses, in the deathly mountains, on the iron-like riverbank, raise the flag of the nation, with the remaining guns and bullets, the surging hot blood, to recover the shattered mountains and rivers.

Shanghai, warm, mysterious, enticing with wine and women; jazz, Citroens, leisurely enjoyment... ignoring day and night... wild embraces on the dance floor, passionate kisses on the screen, everything covered with a gray net, creating a trap of depravity.

The sensational four-corner love movie, showing simultaneously in two theaters, not over at seven o'clock, the nine o'clock audience pushing forward, afraid of falling behind.

In the public column for donating to the Northeast Volunteer Army... "Saving the two copper coins Mom gives me every day, accumulated for two months, offering four corners worth of stamps"; "Sending one yuan for shoes and socks, apprentice XX from XX store"; patriots who dare not fall behind in action.

Citroen, multicolored strange clothes, high heels, affected poses, "Miss, is there anything better?" Pushing aside the socks priced at twenty-five yuan.

Steward, ragged clothes, broken hat, torn shoes, fearful soft voice, "Boss, do a good deed, give me a copper coin to buy congee," he follows behind the gentleman in the Western suit.

Street Promenade

— Tianfang

Deceived by life, I am often on the road. Moved by various feelings, I hastily compose this piece.

(1) Chinese People's Time

Chinese people's time doesn't count for anything. I once counted from Shunxing Clothing Store at the intersection of Fourth Road and Zhejiang Road to Sino-French Pharmacy at the intersection of Shandong Road. Among the seventy-nine clocks, no two showed the same time. The difference ranged from several minutes to more than an hour. Foreigners say Chinese people are like a plate of loose sand. Unexpectedly, Chinese clocks also suffer from this ailment.

(2) Unwritten Constitution

Urinating in alleys is an unwritten constitution. The notice "Urinating Prohibited" is actually equivalent to a "Urinating Allowed" advertisement. Many people find convenience under the implication of this notice.

(3) When China Will Be Strong

When you walk into a small alley, you often step on something under your feet, and that is the residue of medicine. People think it is unlucky to step on medicine residue, as if bringing the illness with them. This has the same wonderful effect as the "Selling Colds" signs on electric poles. Someone asked me when China will be strong? I said, when there is no medicine residue on the streets.

(4) A Scene from the Capital War

Phonographs, gongs and drums, the smell of charcoal, deafening shouts. On every street, there are seventeen or eighteen vendors selling sugar-roasted chestnuts, a scene of the capital war in this world's economic depression.

(5) No Law is Greater Than Police Regulations

Once, I walked along Avenue Edward VII. A rickshaw puller, impatient and disregarding the police officer's baton, rushed across the road. The police officer was furious and tore down his license. The rickshaw puller knelt and begged, but to no avail. As a result, he was led away "into the alley" like a tamed sheep. I was horrified when I saw this. I felt that no law is greater than police regulations, with absolutely no leniency. Look, the League of Nations Covenant cannot deal with Japan, the army, navy, and air force criminal law cannot resolve the civil war, but the police regulations must be strictly obeyed. "The police are truly worthy of admiration," I thought.

(6) The Degree of Sympathy

A big fire burns, watched from across the river; a rickshaw overturns, laughed at with applause. Such is the extent of Chinese people's sympathy!

(7) It's a Pity Her Nose Isn't Higher

Yesterday, I walked past Jing'an Temple Road and encountered two women in front of the Great Shanghai (department store). High-heeled shoes, knee-length dresses, fox fur scarves, felt hats, full of foreign airs, clearly overseas misses. Looking closer, it was a pity their eyes weren't green and their noses weren't higher. Yellow skin and black eyes, truly completely domestically produced. Using silver to imitate countries using gold, I grieve for their fathers, brothers, and husbands!

(8) Shanghai Civilization

Shanghai is a two-thousand-year-old historical museum, a bizarre stage of the twentieth century. Look on the streets, small cars and motorcycles fly side by side, temples and dance halls stand in parallel. When you walk on the street, you feel like you've stepped into a historical museum or watched a historical film. How magnificent! Is this why it's called the Paris of the East?

(9) The Classes of Humanity

There's the difference between the rich living on the twenty-second floor and the temporary concubine sleeping on the cement floor.

At every bridgehead, there are many day laborers waiting. When a rickshaw passes, they help pull it up. From the bottom of the bridge to the top, a copper coin is the price. "Rickshaw pullers must be the lowest class of humanity?" I often think. Yet there are still those who wish to be rickshaw pullers but cannot. Alas! The classes of humanity! Written on November 5, 1932.
