Film Special

New Film Introductions

The "Fight of the Dragon and Tiger" at the Nanjing Grand Theater

— Lin

RKO's colossal beast film, "Fight of the Dragon and Tiger," will likely be released this Thursday at the Nanjing Grand Theater. This hunting film isn't as long as "Human Beasts Wonders" and the plot isn't as complex, but it can stand on its own, creating its own unique style, and possesses characteristics that "Human Beasts Wonders" can't match. Its most outstanding feature is the mutual killing and fighting between tigers, leopards, snakes, rhinos, bulls, elephants, etc. Watching these scenes is breathtaking, and surely many timid people won't dare to watch, or will be frightened, have trouble sleeping at night, have nightmares, etc. Aftereffecto If you don't believe me, let me tell you a story, and you'll believe me;

After RKO produced "Fight of the Dragon and Tiger," Fox also wanted to release a hunting film, reportedly titled "Man Eater." They hired Clive Elliott, the director of "Fight of the Dragon and Tiger," to direct this new film. They also hired a very famous leading actor, whose name, of course, hasn't been announced, and I naturally have no way of knowing. This actor, hearing that he was invited to be the lead in a colossal film and would be traveling to Africa (the film was to be shot in Sumatra), was filled with excitement and readily agreed to a one-year contract without thinking. After signing the contract, he happily went to a cinema to watch a film, and coincidentally, he watched the very film we're about to see, "Fight of the Dragon and Tiger." He was completely terrified from beginning to end. He thought, going to Africa to film wild animals isn't human life. The more he thought, the more frightened he became, and he probably didn't sleep all night. The next morning, he got up and went to the Fox office, waiting for the manager to arrive. Why? Because he said, "I'm not going to Africa. I want to cancel the contract I signed yesterday!"

This film is a meticulously crafted masterpiece by Frank Buck, filmed in the Malay Archipelago. Every foot of it was filmed in Malaya. The most intense part is the snake-tiger fight. A huge, spotted tiger is trapped by a python several feet long, struggling to break free, but the python is also exhausted, and both are eventually captured. Furthermore, the techniques for capturing ferocious beasts and poisonous snakes are incredibly ingenious. If you insist on seeing Wu Song fighting the tiger on Jingyang Ridge, then I won't say anything, but otherwise, "Fight of the Dragon and Tiger" is worth seeing. Also, before seeing this film, I felt that the name was too vulgar, but after seeing it, I felt that the name was extremely appropriate, because the earth-shattering battle between the giant python and the spotted tiger truly deserves the name "Fight of the Dragon and Tiger." But the English title is Bring Em Back Alive. If it were translated as "Capture Alive," wouldn't it be more accurate and less vulgar? I'd like to ask Mr. Lu Shibai what he thinks?

Film Review

A Discussion of "New Firefighting Techniques"

— Yannan

As soon as you see "New Firefighting Techniques" (Fireman, Save My Child) or the Carlton advertisement, you know it's a humorous comedy.

The story is: A baseball star is passionate about firefighting. He often neglects the game because he is too careful and too involved in firefighting. However, in order to marry a girl, he has to give up his job in the fire department and become a baseball player. At the same time, he develops a fast-acting firefighting chemical, achieving both fame and fortune. The team wins the game and he returns triumphantly, marrying her.

The plot is similar to Luke's "Football King" from ten years ago, and the content is comparable to Jack O'Kay's "Silly Football King." Like "Silly Football King," there's a baseball game. In particular, Joe E. Brown, who plays the "firefighting fanatic," his style, actions, and even appearance resemble Jack O'Kay. The plain banana-eating and ball-throwing are all amusing. He is indeed a comedic genius. Evalyn Knapp does a good job. The small subplot of a love triangle gives her room to develop, which is, of course, also the director's ability. The rest of the cast are good supporting characters in this comedy.

If you walk past the Carlton Theater and hear constant laughter, it's all thanks to Brown.

An Hanting's Nationality Problem

— He

An Hanting now has seven cities requesting her to become a citizen. Because her father is a distinguished military officer, often stationed in various places without a fixed residence. If she were to become a citizen of any city, that place would be proud of it.

"Awakening People and the World"!

— Bozhang

Chinese films now, besides romance films and martial arts films, rarely have films that "awaken people and the world"! Apart from one film, "Humanity," there are almost none!

Now we hope that major Chinese film companies will focus their efforts on making more films that "awaken people and the world"! Because if we want to improve Chinese society and the psychology of the people now, I think using films is the best method. Now, slogans have become numb! Lectures are useless! Only films can be screened year after year, and the influence of films on people's psychology is significant, and it is done unconsciously.

However, I also know that it is difficult to gather materials for films that "awaken people and the world," but if you add a bit of romance, it will cater to the psychology of the audience, which is easy to do!

Tianyi Film Company's new sound production, "The Vengeful Spirits," directed by Shao Zuiweng and starring Hu Shan and Ma Loufen, has now been completed.

Local Investigation

Another Visit to Lianhua's First Studio

— Jizhong

Lianhua Company's first studio is the reincarnation of the former Minxin Company. Of course, here we can fully understand how Mr. Li Minwei, the director, sacrifices himself for art. The sale of a large property in the Guangdong area is strong evidence of this.

The reporter visited the first studio. Upon entering, there were countless painters and workers constantly working hard on their respective tasks, orderly, organized, and very serious, without the slightest hint of playfulness.

Director Li Minwei was amiable and approachable, personally receiving us. After exchanging pleasantries, the reporter began to ask him about Lianhua Company's recent plans, the progress of the first studio's new films, and various miscellaneous details. The following is Mr. Li's sincere report:

"Lianhua suffered losses from the January 28th Incident, and internally, we did implement a series of austerity measures. Therefore, at that time, external opinions seemed to suggest that Lianhua might collapse. In reality, this was just speculation. Director Wei Mingyou has worked hard, how could he lightly let it disappear? Now Mr. Luo has returned from Southeast Asia, where he received support and help from overseas Chinese. Perhaps Lianhua will establish another studio there, but nothing has been decided yet. As for our studio (Mr. Li modestly called it), we did feel a lack of directors. There was only Bu Wancang working alone. Now, in order to speed up production and for Mr. Bu's mental rest, we have hired two more directors, Fei Mu, who transferred from the Fifth Studio in Beiping, and Jiang Qifeng, who transferred from Youlian. Currently, in addition to "Modern Three Women" being completely finished, "Childhood China," "City Life," and "Love and Revolution" are being produced simultaneously. Regarding sound films, Lianhua may not produce them for the time being. When the Chinese-made film camera is successfully completed, Lianhua will definitely cooperate with them closely."

Star Biography

Early Life of Tallulah Bankhead (Part 1)

— Meicun

Tallulah Bankhead was born in Alabama, USA, on January 31, 1902. Her young and beautiful mother almost gave up her life to give birth to her. After giving birth, she struggled for three weeks and finally passed away. Before her death, she asked about her two children, Tallulah and her sister Eugenia, saying, "I want to say a few words to them." So the family placed the twenty-one-day-old Tallulah beside her. Eugenia also stood by the bed, her round eyes looking at her mother, seemingly afraid. At this time, she said some sad words, but because no one else was standing in the room, what she said is unknown.

A few minutes later, her husband and family stood around watching her. She said, "Take care of Eugenia, but don't worry about Tallulah, she will take care of herself." This strange and inspired prediction—Tallulah can take care of herself, because her twenty-one days of age is enough to know what she wants—passed in an instant. Year after year, Tallulah grew from a young girl to a young woman. Indeed, she took care of herself and often took care of her sister Eugenia.

Tallulah was a temperamental and imaginative girl. She had a curiosity about everything around her. She could achieve great success in every moment.

Once, she took her grandfather's square-headed cigar and smoked it. He saw her and severely beat her. She felt very resentful. She thought this reprimand was too much, because she was climbing a chestnut tree when she smoked. After smoking this narcotic, she felt dizzy and fell from the chestnut tree. Coincidentally, her grandparents were sitting on chairs under the tree. They saw her and gave her a painful beating. Was it fair to be beaten after already suffering from smoking that "damn thing"?

Her temper was very bad. When she wanted something and couldn't get it, she would grab anything and throw it around. She would also lie on the floor, cover her ears with both hands, face down, and roll back and forth, making a fuss. Her black nanny would often be frightened, looking up and shouting loudly, "Miss Tallulah is having a tantrum again! Come and help me lift her up." In a moment, the whole family would rush to help her up, pat the dirt off her, and tell her to be quiet, until her doting aunt or strict grandparents gave her candy, and then she would stop crying. She often had these naughty and brave episodes. But she also came to her senses quickly and soon became precocious. In this era, she didn't like playing with children, she only liked being with adults. When she came to the house, she knocked on the door very respectfully. Her aunt heard her and asked, "Who is it?" She would answer in a soft voice, "It's Tallulah," and then open the door and come in.

During her childhood, Tallulah suffered from tonsillitis and bronchitis for several years. This is why it is said that she had a low vision. (To be continued)

Rare News from the Film Industry

Her Special Profession: Shouting

— Ziyin

When recording sound films, when there is a scene of fear, the sound of a scream must be recorded. But not every star has a strong voice. Many big stars can't scream. Constance Bennett can't scream. Ruth Chatterton and Anne Francis also can't scream. As a result, a woman named Alice Doll has a special profession.

For example, when Bennett is in a murder scene, she has many screaming actions, but in reality, she doesn't make a sound.

Bennett said, "The sound I make when I scream is just 'eek.' If I really try to scream, I won't be able to speak for a few takes."

Her director quickly said, "Don't scream, it's too much of a loss. Alice Doll can scream for you."

Indeed, damaging a star's voice during filming is a great loss to the company. Many people will become hoarse from shouting too much. But there are also people like Alice Doll who can scream continuously without hurting their vocal cords. So she becomes a substitute for many famous stars in Hollywood.

She can also change her scream to suit the personality and vocal tone of the person she's replacing. Someone like her can't be considered anything less than a special profession.

The Screenwriter's Joke

— Bin

The following story happened in Hollywood, USA. In the American film industry, there was a person who ran a film business. One day, he went to ask a screenwriter to write a script for him, and the content of the script had to include the following four things:

(1) Contains religious significance;

(2) Contains aristocratic elements;

(3) Contains sexual thoughts;

(4) Contains an element of fright.

In a few days, the screenwriter finished the script, but the filmmaker was confused when he saw it. It turned out that the script was very short, and its content said: "My God!" the Duchess cried, "take away your hand off my legs.”

The filmmaker went to consult the screenwriter. The screenwriter smiled and replied, "It's very easy to explain! You see, isn't 'God' of religious significance? Isn't the Duchess aristocratic? The lady asked the man to take his hand off her leg, isn't that sexual? Doesn't the Duchess's tone have a sudden element of fright? I've depicted all four things you wanted!"

So the filmmaker couldn't help but laugh.

Film Treatise

Like Horses in a Circus

— Chen Dabei

Acting in movies is different from acting in stage plays. In stage plays, the expressions of the actors progress gradually from the opening to the closing. Movies are different. When filming a movie, it is not filmed in order. The most patient director will tell you at most, "Now we are going to shoot the number shot. This shot is a close-up. You are angry because you have been offended by so and so. Now you have to grit your teeth and be angry." People who are used to acting on stage will feel that this kind of command is very unconscious. But you have to understand that movie actors are not acting there, they are taking pictures there. A movie is nothing more than many consecutive photos being shot back and forth into film, and then re-edited in order.

Therefore, people who are movie actors must have a greater ability to express emotions than stage actors. To use horses as a metaphor. The work of stage actors is like the work of horses in horse races or horses on the front lines. Although their work is not out of their own intentions, they can still get a little bit of nearly natural interest. The work of movie actors is like horses in a circus. It is difficult for him to get the opportunity to develop free will.

For this reason, when you practice, you must practice all kinds of facial expressions to the point where they come at will and are dismissed at will, so that you will not panic and be unable to deal with it after hearing the director's command.

When practicing the second style, keeping the state of anger, breathing can indeed help you achieve the tense emotions of anger, but your imagination must take on a large part of the work. You have to be able to imagine that the person in the mirror is your father's enemy, the one who hurt you, or, to put it bluntly, the rival who took your lover, and your resentment will naturally be realistic.
